الحركة والسكون الاختياريين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A capable agent can be devoid of all action indefinitely.
Correction: Rational necessity shows that a capable agent must perform an act or its opposite; permanent inaction is impossible.

Checkpoint

C) The agent has power but does not act.
D) The agent's speech is uncreated.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila claim that a capable agent can be permanently devoid of action is rationally impossible and demolishes their school.

?

?

Are you using your capacities for what they were intended, or are you living as if inaction is permissible? Divine Speech: Single Attribute or Multiple Acts?
Contrasts Sunni and Mu'tazilī views on divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni and Mu'tazilī views on the nature of divine speech and how they affect the relationship between command and prohibition.

Core Idea
Divine speech is either one attribute or many acts—this changes everything.

This passage presents a sharp critique of a mutakallim who holds that a command only implies dislike of its opposite, not prohibition. The author then questions this person's deeper assumption about the nature of divine speech. Two opposing views emerge: the Sunni position that speech is a single uncreated attribute, and the Mu'tazilī position that it consists of created letters and sounds. The choice between these views determines whether command and prohibition can be one and the same or must be distinct.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author first states the mutakallim's position, then poses a dilemma about the nature of divine speech.
The passage ends abruptly; focus on the core contrast presented.
2
Identify the two views on divine speech
Find where the author contrasts the Sunni and Mu'tazilī views. Note the key phrases: 'معنى قائم بالذات' vs 'حروف منظومة وأصوات مقطوعة'.
3
Understand the implications for command and prohibition
Reflect on why the nature of speech matters: if speech is a single attribute, then command and prohibition can coexist in that one attribute; if speech is composed of separate acts, then a command cannot be a prohibition.
This connects to the mutakallim's earlier claim about command and dislike.
4
Answer the checkpoint question
Test your understanding by answering the multiple-choice question. It directly asks about the difference between the two views as presented in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن بعض المتكلمين ممن تكلم في أصول الفقه من أهل ديارنا ذكر أني أقول : إن الأمر بالشيء يقتضي كراهة ضده لا نهيه و لا أقول إنه نهى عن ضده ولا أقول إنه يدل على نهيه ولا أنه يقتضي نهيًا . ولست أدري ماذا كان رأيه في الكلام؟ أنه هو المعنى القائم بالذات المنافي للسكوت والآفة وهو بعينه أمر بما أمر به نهي عما نهى عنه كما هو مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة. أو هو هذه الحروف المنظومة والأصوات المقطوعة ، وما كان أمرًا لا يكون نهيًا، وما كان نهيًا لا يكون أمرًا كما هو مذهب المعتزلة ؟ وكذا ما كان رأيه أن توجه الوعيد...
Then one of the mutakallimūn who spoke on uṣūl al-fiqh from the people of our region mentioned that I say: the command of a thing requires dislike (karāha) of its opposite, not its prohibition; and I do not say that it is a prohibition of its opposite, nor do I say that it indicates its prohibition, nor that it requires a prohibition. But I do not know what his opinion was about [divine] speech (al-kalām): Is it the meaning subsisting in the essence, incompatible with silence and defect, and it is itself a command for what it commands and a prohibition for what it prohibits, as is the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jamāʿa? Or is it these arranged letters and segmented sounds, such that what is a command cannot be a prohibition and what is a prohibition cannot be a command, as is the doctrine of the Muʿtazila? And likewise, what was his opinion about the direction of the threat (tawajjuh al-waʿīd)...
Source pages p. 833

Commentary
This passage criticizes a mutakallim who holds that a command only implies dislike (karāha) of its opposite, not actual prohibition. The author then questions this person's view on the nature of divine speech (kalām): either it is a single attribute subsisting in God's essence (the Sunni view), in which case it is inherently both command and prohibition; or it is composed of letters and sounds (the Muʿtazilī view), in which case command and prohibition are separate and cannot be the same. The passage ends abruptly with a question about the direction of the threat (tawajjuh al-waʿīd), leaving the argument incomplete.

Correction: The Sunni view holds that divine speech is a single, eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, which encompasses both command and prohibition. The Mu'tazilī view divides it into separate created entities.

The Proof Against Pre-Existent Power
Proof that pre-existent power necessitates independence from God, contradicting divine lordship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi school holds that power (qudra) does not precede the action, and why pre-existent power leads to theologically unacceptable consequences.

Core Idea
Pre-existent power contradicts total dependence on Allah.

This passage presents a key Maturidi proof against the view that power exists before the action. The author argues that if power were pre-existent, the servant would be independent of Allah at the moment of action, which is tantamount to disbelief. He also points to the constant need for divine assistance as evidence that humans are always dependent. Understanding this argument is crucial for grasping the Maturidi position on human power and divine omnipotence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow before interpreting.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the main claim and proof
Find the central thesis: pre-existent power leads to independence from God. Notice how the author presents it as a famous proof.
3
Understand the logical chain
Trace the logic: pre-existent power → servant independent at time of action → this is kufr. Ask why this is considered disbelief.
The author equates independence from God with disbelief.
4
Examine the consensus argument
The author mentions the consensus of Ahl al-Qibla on asking for assistance (al-mu'wana) and seeking success (al-tawfiq). Reflect on why this consensus is evidence against pre-existent power.
If power were given beforehand, such requests would be meaningless.
5
Note the reference to Imam Abu Mansur
The author notes that Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi provided deeper arguments. Recognize that the author omits details to avoid prolixity.
This shows the depth of the Maturidi tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقدم القدرة على الفعل يؤدي إلى الاستغناء عن الله:
ومن مشاهير الدلائل لنا في المسألة: أن القول بتقدم القدرة على الفعل يوجب استفتاء العهد عن الله تعالى وقت الفعل والقول بغنية العبد عن الله تعالى في لحظة من عمره كفر. وكذا إجماع أهل القبلة على سؤال المعونة وطلب التوفيق من الله تعالى في كل وقت، ولو كان الإنسان أعطى قدرة الطاعة قبل وجودها لم يكن للطلب معنى.
وراء ذلك طرق كثيرة أوردها أئمتنا أبو منصور – رحمه الله – في تقريرها ودفع الأسئلة عنها، واعتمد على أن إعطاء القدرة قبل الفعل خروج عن الحكمة، ولا يليق ذلك بحكمة الباري عز وجل، وبالغ فيه مبالغة عظيمة استقصى في تحقيقها ودفع الأسئلة عنها أعرضنا عن ذكر ذلك كله مخافة التطويل، والله الموفق.
The pre-existence of power over action leads to independence from God:
And among the famous proofs for us in this issue: that the statement that power precedes action necessitates making the servant independent of God at the time of action, and saying that the servant is independent of God at any moment of his life is disbelief. Similarly, the consensus of the people of the Qibla on asking for assistance and seeking success from God at every time. And if the human being had been given the power of obedience before its existence, the request would have no meaning. Beyond that are many methods that our imams have mentioned, and our teacher Imam Abu Mansur may God have mercy on him, in establishing them and repelling questions about them, and he relied on the fact that giving power before action is contrary to wisdom, and that is not befitting the wisdom of the Exalted Creator. And he deeply emphasized that, going to great lengths in verifying it and repelling questions about it. We have refrained from mentioning all of that for fear of prolixity. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 834

Commentary
This passage presents a proof against the Mu'tazilite claim that power (qudra) precedes the action. The author first states the title: 'Pre-existence of power over action leads to independence from God.' He then gives a famous proof: if power precedes the action, the servant becomes independent of God at the moment of action, which is disbelief (kufr). Furthermore, the consensus of Ahl al-Qibla on constantly asking God for assistance and success shows that humans are always in need of God's help. If the power for obedience were given before the act, such requests would be meaningless. The author then notes that Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi provided detailed arguments for this position, emphasizing that granting power before the act is contrary to divine wisdom. The author refrains from elaborating fully to avoid excessive length. The overall argument is that pre-existent power undermines the servant's dependence on God and contradicts both divine wisdom and the practice of supplication.

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Interpretation of 'Take with Strength'
Refutation of Mu'tazilite proof from Quran for pre-existent power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that the verse 'Take what We have given you with strength' proves pre-existent power, by demonstrating that strength must exist at the time of the action.

Core Idea
Strength must exist at the moment of the act, not before.

The author now turns to refuting specific Quranic proofs used by the Mu'tazila. One key verse is 'Take what We have given you with strength.' The Mu'tazila claim this implies power exists before the act, but careful analysis shows the opposite: strength must be present when the action occurs, and it cannot persist from an earlier time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Notice how the author first reinterprets general verses about pre-existent capacity before focusing on the specific verse.
The passage is dense; take your time with the logical steps.
2
Identify the two interpretations
The Mu'tazila interpret 'Take with strength' as indicating power before the act. The author argues it means strength at the time of the act. Locate where each interpretation is presented.
3
Understand the logical argument
The author uses a conditional: if strength were absent at the time of taking, it wouldn't be 'taking with strength.' He also argues that if strength preceded, it would have to persist, which is impossible for accidents. Follow this reasoning.
This is a key argument in the broader debate on qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونصرف العناية بعد هذا إلى دفع شبهات الخصوم وحل إشكالاتهم فنقول وبالله المعونة:
ما تتعلق به المعتزلة من الآيات التي فيها إشارة إلى تقدم الاستطاعة، محمول على الاستطاعة الأولى التي هي سلامة الأسباب وصحة الآلات، وقوله تعالى: (خُذُوا مَا آتَيْنَاكُم بِقُوَّةٍ) دليلنا؛ لأنه إنما يصير أخذا بالقوة إذا كانت القوة وقت الأخذ موجودة، فأما إذا كانت هي معدومة وقت الأخذ فلا يكون أخذا بقوة كالأخذ باليد، ثم ليس من ضرورة الأخذ بالقوة تقدمها على الأخذ بل وجودها عند الأخذ، ومن ضرورة وجودها عند الأخذ أن لا تكون موجودة قبله لاستحالة بقائها. على أن أهل التأويل قالوا: (خُذُوا مَا آتَيْنَاكُم بِقُوَّةٍ) أي: بجد ومواظبة.
And we turn attention after this to refuting the doubts of the opponents and resolving their difficulties. So we say, and with God is assistance: What the Mu'tazila cling to from the verses that indicate the pre-existence of capacity (istita'a) is interpreted as referring to the first capacity which is the safety of means and health of instruments. And His saying, the Exalted: 'Take what We have given you with strength' is our proof; because one only becomes a taker with strength if the strength exists at the time of taking. But if it is non-existent at the time of taking, then it is not taking with strength, like taking with the hand. Then it is not a necessary condition of taking with strength that strength precede the taking; rather, its existence at the time of taking is sufficient. And from the necessity of its existence at the time of taking is that it does not exist before it, because of the impossibility of its persistence. Moreover, the people of ta'wil said: 'Take what We have given you with strength' means with seriousness and perseverance.
Source pages p. 835

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite use of Quranic verses to argue that capacity (istita'a) precedes the action. The author first reinterprets such verses: they refer to the initial capacity of safety and health, not the power for the act itself. He then focuses on the verse 'Take what We have given you with strength' and uses it as proof for his own position. The reasoning is that 'taking with strength' requires the strength to exist at the moment of taking; if strength were absent at that time, the action would not be truly 'with strength'. Therefore, strength must be simultaneous with the act, not prior. Moreover, if strength preceded the act, it would need to persist until the act, but accidents cannot persist. The author also mentions that some interpreters (ahl al-ta'wil) explain the verse metaphorically as meaning 'with seriousness and perseverance', further distancing it from a literal pre-existent power. The overall argument is that the Quranic evidence actually supports the view that power is contemporaneous with the act.

Key Terms
استطاعة
قوة
أخذ
تقدم
بقاء
تأويل
جد
مواظبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Take what We have given you with strength' implies that power must exist before the action.
Correction: The author shows that the verse actually requires strength to be present at the time of the action, not before. If strength were absent at the moment of taking, the action would not be 'with strength'.

Checkpoint
How does the author interpret the verse 'Take what We have given you with strength'?
A) It indicates that strength must precede the act.
B) It means strength must exist at the time of the act.
C) It refers to physical strength.
D) It is about financial stability.

Key Takeaway
The verse 'Take with strength' proves that power must be present at the time of action, not before.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'Take what We have given you with strength', do you assume you will have the strength later, or do you pray for strength at the very moment of action? This lesson demands that you rely on God's immediate giving. Will you begin each action with a plea for strength now?
?
The Mu'tazila used a verse to support their view, but the author showed they misinterpreted it. Is there an area of your faith where you might be twisting scripture to fit what you want to believe? Ask yourself honestly and repent.
?
The author argues that strength cannot precede the act because accidents cannot persist. Your own good deeds are accidents that depend on God's creation at each moment. Does this humble you to know that you have no independent store of power? How will you change your reliance on God today?

Ash'ari on the Permissibility of Taklif Ma La Yutaq
Nasafi reports Ash'ari's justification for the obligation of what cannot be borne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari justifies the rational permissibility of obligating what cannot be borne, based on God's absolute sovereignty and the nature of human commands.

Core Idea
What is unjust for a human can be just for God, because God owns all dominion.

Al-Ash'ari addresses a challenging theological question: Could God command something impossible, like combining two opposites? In this passage, he argues that such obligation is rationally permissible for God, even if it seems unreasonable for humans. The key lies in understanding the difference between a human commander and God, the true Owner of all.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how Ash'ari builds his argument from a bold claim to a nuanced justification.
The passage is dense with theological reasoning.
2
Identify Ash'ari's main claim
Find where Ash'ari states that obligating the impossible is permissible (ja'iz) and note the example of combining two opposites.
This is the central thesis of the passage.
3
Understand the key distinction
Ash'ari contrasts human and divine commandments. Notice why he thinks ugliness (qubh) applies to humans but not to God: because God acts in His own dominion and is beyond need.
This is the core of his justification.
4
Reflect on the sign theory
Pay attention to how Ash'ari reinterprets obedience and disobedience as signs (amarat) of God's will for reward or punishment, not as causes of entitlement.
This supports why God can make an impossible command a sign of punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فذكر الأشعري في كتابه المسمى بالنوادر أن تكليف ما لا يطاق جائز، وأن الله تعالى لو أمر عبده بالجمع بين الضدين لم يكن سفها ولا مستحيلاً، وهذا على أصله مستقيم فإن من أصله أن الله تعالى لو عذب الخلق في النيران خالدًا مخلدًا من غير جناية وجدت منهم كان ذلك حكمة وصوابًا؛ لأنه يتصرف في ملكه وكون تكليف ما لا يطاق في الشاهد إنما كان قبيحا لأن المكلف لا يتصرف في ملك نفسه، ولأن المكلف في الشاهد يأمر لجلب نفع وينهى لدفع ضرر، ولا يحصل ذلك بتكليف ما ليس في الوسع بخلاف الصانع جل جلاله فإنه يَجِلَّ عن جلب نفع أو دفع ضرر، ولا استحقاق من العبد لا للجنة ولا للنار بفعله وإنما الطاعة والمعصية أمارتان يستدل بهما، أن الله تعالى يعذب هذا في النار ويدخل ذلك الجنة، فعلى هذا لو كلف العبد ما لا يطاق ويجعل ذلك أمارة أنه معاقب كان ذلك جائزاً، وإذا كان كذلك كان تكليف العبد ما ليست له قدرة عليه لاشتغاله بضده جائزاً غير أن الشرع ورد بتكليف هذا النوع، ولم يرد بتكليف ذلك النوع مع استوائهما في الجواز.
Al-Ash'ari mentioned in his book called al-Nawadir that the obligation of what cannot be borne is permissible, and that if God Almighty commanded His servant to combine two opposites, it would not be foolishness nor impossible. This is consistent with his principle, for it is his principle that if God Almighty were to punish creation eternally in the fires without any sin committed by them, that would be wisdom and correct, because He acts in His dominion. And the fact that obligation of what cannot be borne is considered ugly in this world is because the one who obliges does not act in his own self's dominion, and because the one who obliges in this world commands to attract benefit and forbids to repel harm, and that is not achieved by obliging what is beyond capacity, unlike the Maker, may His majesty be exalted, for He is far above attracting benefit or repelling harm. There is no entitlement from the servant to either Paradise or Fire by his action; rather, obedience and disobedience are signs by which it is inferred that God Almighty will punish this one in the Fire and admit that one to Paradise. Based on this, if He obligated the servant what he cannot bear and made that a sign that he is to be punished, that would be permissible. And if that is so, then obliging the servant with something for which he has no power due to being occupied with its opposite is permissible, except that the Law came with obliging this type and did not come with obliging that type, even though they are equal in permissibility.
Source pages p. 840

Commentary
This passage reports Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's position on the issue of taklif ma la yutaq (obligation of what cannot be borne). Ash'ari holds that such obligation is permissible (ja'iz) for God, even if it involves commanding something impossible like combining two opposites. He argues that what makes an obligation 'ugly' (qabih) in the human context is that the human commander acts outside his own dominion or seeks personal benefit, whereas God owns all dominion and is above any need for benefit or harm. Moreover, reward and punishment are not based on the servant's own merit but are determined by God's decree; obedience and disobedience are merely signs (amarat) that indicate His will. Therefore, God could command what is impossible and make that command a sign of punishment—this is within His prerogative. However, Ash'ari notes that the revealed Law (shar') has actually commanded one type (possible obligations) and not the other, even though both are equally possible for God. Thus, the distinction is not based on inherent rational impossibility but on what God has chosen to legislate.

Key Terms
تكليف ما لا يطاق
جائز
ملك
أمارة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Ash'ari's view implies divine injustice or that God acts arbitrarily.
Correction: Ash'ari denies that humans have any entitlement to reward or punishment; God's actions are always wise and just because He is the absolute owner. The ugliness of impossible commands in human context does not apply to God.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Ash'ari, why is taklif ma la yutaq not considered ugly (qabih) for God?
A) Because God is not bound by any laws.
B) Because God acts in His own dominion and does not seek benefit or avoid harm.
C) Because it is impossible for God to command what is beyond capacity.
D) Because the Law never permits such obligation.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari's position is that God's obligation of the impossible is rationally permissible because God is the absolute owner and is beyond seeking benefit, and the revealed Law simply chose not to command it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that you deserve nothing from God—neither reward nor punishment—how would your daily acts of worship change? Would you obey out of love or fear, or what would motivate you?
?
When you face a command from Allah that seems beyond your strength, do you trust that He knows your limits better than you do? Or do you resent Him for demanding what you cannot give?
?
Ash'ari says your obedience is merely a sign—not the cause—of God's reward. Does that make you feel less responsible for your actions, or does it humble you to realize your efforts are not what earn you Paradise? How will you respond?

The Jabr View of Jahm on Human Actions
Introduces the Jabr position on divine vs. human creation of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Jabr position—its denial of human power over actions and its claim that attributing actions to humans is merely metaphorical.

Core Idea
For Jahm, human actions are as involuntary as a heartbeat.

Having established the framework for capacity (istita'a), the author now turns to the central debate: are our actions truly ours or merely attributed to us? The first view presented is the extreme determinism of Jahm b. Safwan, which denies any real human power and treats all actions as coercive.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the overall claim.
Pay attention to the analogy of involuntary movements.
2
Identify the key claim of Jahm
The passage states that some people ascribe all actions to God, deny human control, and even deny that humans have any power. This is the Jabr view.
3
Understand the analogy
Jahm compares human actions to involuntary movements like trembling or pulse beats—things over which a person has no control.
This analogy shows that for Jabr, all actions are forced.
4
Contrast with metaphorical attribution
Notice that for Jahm, saying 'Zayd went' is like saying 'the boy grew tall'—a statement that describes an event, not an act of free will.
This highlights the radical difference from views that affirm human agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث الكلام في خلق أفعال العباد: وإذ فرغنا من بيان الاستطاعة وإثباتها وأقسامها ، ووقت ثبوت كل منها فنتجاوز إلى الكلام في أفعال العباد أنها مخلوقة لهم أم الله تعالى؟ فنقول – وبالله التوفيق: قول جهم وأتباعه بالجبر: اختلف الناس في أفعال الخلق جعلها بعضهم الله تعالى، ونفوا عنها تدبير الخلق وأزالوا عنها قدرتهم بل لم يثبتوا لهم قدرة، وجعلوها كلها اضطرارية كحركات المرتعش وحركات العروق النابضة، وأحالوا اتصاف العباد بالقدرة وهو قول جهم بن صفوان الترمذي، وإضافتها إلى العباد عند هؤلاء مجاز، فيكون قول القائل : ذهب زید و مشى عمرو بمنزلة قول القائل طال الغلام ومات زيد وأبيض شعر عمر وشاخ عبد الله.
Chapter Three: Discourse on the Creation of the Actions of Servants: And when we have finished explaining the capacity (istita'a), its affirmation, its divisions, and the time of each of them, we proceed to discourse on the actions of servants—whether they are created for them or for God? So we say—and with God is success: The statement of Jahm and his followers on compulsion: People differed concerning the actions of creation. Some of them ascribed them to God, denied the servants' control over them, removed their power from them, indeed did not affirm power for them, and made them all coercive like the movements of a trembling person and the movements of pulsating veins. They deemed impossible the description of servants with power. This is the statement of Jahm b. Safwan al-Tirmidhi. Attribution of actions to servants according to these [thinkers] is metaphorical, so the statement of the speaker: 'Zayd went' and 'Amr walked' is like the statement: 'The boy grew tall' and 'Zayd died' and 'Umar's hair turned white' and 'Abdullah aged.'
Source pages p. 849

Commentary
This passage is a definition and exposition of the Jabr (compulsion) position attributed to Jahm b. Safwan. It begins by transitioning from the previous discussion on capacity (istita'a) to the new topic of whether actions are created for servants or for God. The author then states that people differed: some attribute all actions to God, denying any human control, power, or capacity. They analogize human actions to involuntary movements like trembling or pulse. They consider describing a servant as having power to be impossible. Thus, for Jahm and his followers, any attribution of an action to a person is purely metaphorical, comparable to saying a boy grew tall or a man died—things over which the individual has no control. This section sets up the contrast with the Mu'tazilite position that follows.

Correction: In Jabr, humans have no power or role in their actions; actions are directly created by God and merely attributed to humans metaphorically, unlike the Ash'ari kasb which affirms a form of human acquisition.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Jabr view of Jahm denies any real human power over actions, treating all human acts as purely metaphorical attributions of events caused solely by God.

?

?

The Sunni Doctrine of Divine Attributes
The author concludes that Allah's attributes are known from His self-description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that Allah's attributes are known only through His own self-description, not through human reason or speculation.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are defined by Allah alone, not by human reasoning.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla concludes a discussion on divine attributes. The author asserts that the proper knowledge of Allah's attributes comes solely from how Allah has described Himself in revelation, grounding the methodology of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. This principle safeguards against both anthropomorphism and negation of attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own phrasing come through before interpretation.
2
Note the Quranic references

The first is incomplete in the text; the second is from Surah az-Zumar:62.
3
Identify the core claim
The passage states that we benefit knowledge that Allah is described with what He described Himself. This is the central Sunni principle for knowing Allah's attributes.
4
Recognize the designation
The author declares this to be the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, indicating it is the orthodox position.
5
Reflect on the implication
This methodology prevents both excess (tashbih) and deficiency (ta'til) in understanding Allah. Think about why this is important.

This is the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a.

Commentary
This passage concludes a prior discussion. The author states that through the realization of Allah's statement about His grace and mercy, we benefit from the second point (likely referring to a preceding enumeration) knowledge that Allah is described with what He described Himself and praised with that. He then quotes the verse 'Creator of all things, and He is over all things a Guardian' (az-Zumar 62) as evidence. He declares this to be the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a.

Specification of the General Verse: God's Essence and Attributes
Nasafi argues that the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay' does not include God's essence or attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' cannot be used to claim that God's essence and attributes are created, and the principles of specification (takhsis) in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Including God's essence in 'everything' would contradict the verse's purpose.

This lesson examines Nasafi's argument that the Qur'anic verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything' does not encompass God's own essence or attributes. At first glance, the verse seems universally inclusive, but Nasafi shows that linguistic generality must be interpreted in light of the verse's purpose. He then discusses the usul principle that a specified general term ('amm makhsus') becomes ambiguous for doctrinal certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Try to grasp Nasafi's main flow of argument before diving into details.
2
Identify the main claim
What is Nasafi trying to prove? He asserts that the verse does not include God's essence and attributes. Note the reason he gives: including them would nullify the very purpose of the verse.
3
Understand the principle of specification
Nasafi explains that even though the word 'everything' could linguistically include essence and attributes, they are excluded because their inclusion would lead to a contradiction. He also discusses the rule of consistency: if something is excluded for a reason, anything sharing that reason must also be excluded.
This is a key principle in usul al-fiqh called takhsis.
4
Consider the epistemological status
Nasafi notes that a specified general term becomes ambiguous (mujmal) for many scholars, and in doctrinal matters, only certain knowledge is acceptable. Thus, relying on such a verse is insufficient.
5
Conclude the lesson
Reflect on how Nasafi's argument shows that general verses must be interpreted within their intended scope, and that theological disputes cannot be settled by mere linguistic generality.
This reinforces the importance of usul methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جميع ما يحققه أن ذات الله تعالى شيء بلا خلاف بيننا وبينكم، وكذا صفاته عند كثير منكم أشياء ولم تكن ذاته ولا صفاته عند كثير منكم أشياء، ولم تكن ذاته ولا صفاته داخلاً تحت هذه الآية لما في دخول ذلك فيها زوال ما سبقت له الآية من إثبات ما كان دخوله تحت الخطاب يوجب إبطال الفرض الذي سيق له الخطاب ويثبت ضد ذلك يمتنع دخوله تحته، وإن كان بحيث يتناوله اللفظ من حيث اللغة، وإن لم يخص شيء سواه مما يتناوله لفظ الخطاب فكيف وقد خص منه غيره مما هو مساو لذلك الغير في المعنى الموجب خروجه عن قضية الكلام، ولا شك أن إخراج بعض ما يتناوله اللفظ عن وضعه لمعنى يوجب إخراجه موجب إخراج يوجد فيه ذلك المعنى لاقتضاء القول التسوية في الحكم عند ثبوت المساواة في المعنى الموجب لذلك، على أن العام الذي خص منشئ يتوقف فيه عند كثير من أهل الأصول لصيرورته مجملاً، ولا يصح التعلق به لإثبات حكم جار مجرى الفروع يمكن إثباته بما لا وجه إلى إثباتها إلا الدليل القاطع الموجب للعلم الثابت بطريق التيقن، وعند أكثر أهل الأصول وإن لم ينقلب مجملاً إلا أنه يجب الحكم فيما وراء المخصوص من أفراد العموم وأحاده بطريق التيقن، بل يوجب ذلك بطريق غالب الرأي بلا خلاف بيننا وبينكم على أن هذا عندكم حكم العام وإن لم يخص منه شيء، والتعلق بمثل هذا الدليل في الأبواب الاعتقادية جهل بمواضع الحجاج ومواقع الأدلة ومراتبها في أنفسها ودرجات المحال التي يتعلق بها فيها، ويتبين بهذا أن لا متعلق بالآية في محل النزاع وموضع الخلاف.
What he verifies is that the essence of God, exalted, is a thing without disagreement between us and you, and likewise His attributes are things according to many of you, and His essence and attributes were not included under this verse, because in their inclusion in it would be the removal of what the verse was intended to establish; what its inclusion under the discourse would necessitate invalidating the premise for which the discourse was set and would establish the opposite of that, so its inclusion under it is prohibited, even if it is such that the word includes it from a linguistic perspective, and even if nothing else among what the word of the discourse includes has been specified, how [can it be included] when other than it has been specified from it, which is equal to that other in the meaning necessitating its exclusion from the purport of the speech; and there is no doubt that the exclusion of some of what the word includes from its position for a meaning that necessitates its exclusion necessitates the exclusion of that in which that meaning is found, because the statement requires equality in the ruling when equality is established in the meaning necessitating that, especially since the general term that has been specified becomes problematic for many of the scholars of usul due to its becoming ambiguous, and it is not valid to rely on it to establish a ruling that runs in the course of derivative matters, which can be established by nothing that has no way to establish it except the conclusive evidence that necessitates certain knowledge established by the path of certainty; and according to most of the scholars of usul, even if it does not become ambiguous, the ruling concerning the remaining individuals of the general term and its particulars must be established by the path of certainty; rather it necessitates that by the path of predominant opinion without disagreement between us and you, provided that this is with you the ruling of the general even if nothing has been specified from it; and relying on such evidence in the doctrinal chapters is ignorance of the positions of argument, the locations of evidences, their own ranks, and the degrees of the matters that are attached to them; and by this it becomes clear that there is no reliance on the verse in the locus of dispute and the place of disagreement.
Source pages p. 859

Commentary
This passage is an argument that the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay' (Allah is the Creator of everything) does not include God's own essence and attributes. Nasafi begins by stating that there is no dispute between Muslims and their opponents that God's essence is a thing. Similarly, according to many of the opponents, God's attributes are also things. However, neither His essence nor His attributes fall under the general term of this verse. The reason is that including them would nullify the very purpose for which the verse was revealed, which is to affirm that God creates everything other than Himself, and to negate the claim that anything else creates. If the essence and attributes were included, it would imply that they are created, which is false. Even though the word 'everything' linguistically could encompass them, they must be specified out because including them would contradict the intended meaning. Nasafi then discusses the principle of specification (takhsis) of general terms: if a general term is specified for a rational meaning, any item that shares that meaning should also be excluded for consistency. Moreover, many usul scholars hold that a specified general term becomes ambiguous and cannot be used to establish certain rulings in secondary matters; at best it gives probable knowledge. In doctrinal matters, only certain evidence is acceptable, so relying on this verse in this context shows ignorance of proper argumentation. The conclusion is that the verse provides no support for the opponents' position in this dispute.

Key Terms
ذات
صفات
عموم
خصوص
تخصيص
مجمل
تيقن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Khaliq kulli shay' is absolutely universal and includes everything, even God's essence and attributes.
Correction: Nasafi argues that inclusion would contradict the verse's purpose (to establish God as the sole creator of other things), so it is excluded despite linguistic generality.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi argue that the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay' does not include God's essence and attributes?
A) Because the Arabic word 'kull' does not actually mean 'all'.
B) Because including them would nullify the praise intended by the verse and imply they are created.
C) Because God's essence and attributes are not things.
D) Because the verse was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
A general verse may be specified by its purpose, and cannot be used to prove points about God's essence and attributes in doctrinal matters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay', do you ever stop to consider what 'everything' truly means in light of God's own essence? Have you assumed a verse includes all without examining its context and purpose? How will you change your approach to Quranic interpretation after learning that even a general verse can be limited by its intended meaning?
?
This lesson warns against using a specified general term as certain proof in matters of creed. Are there beliefs you hold that you have never examined the certainty of their evidence? Are you willing to test your convictions against the level of proof required for doctrinal matters? What would it mean for you to base your faith on certain knowledge rather than common understandings?
?
Nasafi says relying on such evidence is 'ignorance of the positions of argument'. When have you used a proof text without understanding its context and limitations? Will you commit to studying the principles of deriving correct creed from revelation, rather than accepting surface readings? What concrete step will you take this week to deepen your understanding of how to properly interpret divine speech?

Nasafi's Refutation of the Impossibility of Creating Acts
Nasafi refutes three proofs of impossibility using the verse and rational distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the objection that God cannot create ugly acts by distinguishing between the moral status of acts and the act of creation itself.

Core Idea
Creating something ugly is not itself ugly; wisdom is in bringing things about as they should be.

Nasafi responds to an objection that would limit God's power: if God cannot create ugly acts, then the verse 'Allah is the Creator of all things' would be false. He systematically addresses three potential proofs of impossibility—divine wisdom, shared power, and ugliness—showing each fails. This lesson unpacks his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Context of the objection
Understand why someone would object that God cannot create ugly acts (e.g., insulting God).
The objection is based on the idea that a wise God would not create something morally repugnant.
2
Nasafi's opening argument from the verse
See how Nasafi uses the verse 'Allah is the Creator of all things' to argue that if creating acts were impossible, it would equate God with creatures and remove the praise intended by the verse.
3
Three responses to possible proofs of impossibility
Walk through each argument (divine wisdom, shared power, ugliness) and Nasafi's reply. Note that he shifts the burden of proof onto the opponent.
Nasafi's responses are cumulative; each addresses a different angle.
4
Key distinction: creating vs. created act
Grasp the crucial point that moral categories apply to the created act, not to the act of creation itself. Creating something ugly is not subject to the same moral judgment.
This is the most important conceptual move.
5
Promise of fuller explanation
Nasafi indicates that he will provide a more detailed rational argument later. This shows that the present argument is part of a larger discourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورود الآية يدل أن دخول أفعال الخلق ليس بمستحيل لأن جعل ذلك مستحيلاً يوجب التسوية بينه وبين ما دب ودرج وذا يزيل معنى التمدح الذي سيقت له الآية، على أنا نسألهم عن دليل الاستحالة فإن قالوا: دليل استحالة ذلك كون الباري حكيمًا فلا يليق به تخليق شتم نفسه، فقد أجبنا عنه، وإن جعلوا دليل الاستحالة دخول مقدور تحت قدرة قادرين فنقول : مورد الآية يقتضي نفي الاستحالة لما في ثبوت استحالة زوال معنى التمدح على أنا نبين أن ذلك ليس بمستحيل إذا شرعنا في المعقول إن شاء الله تعالى - على أن إقامة دليل الاستحالة عليهم لا علينا، وإن جعلوا دليل الاستحالة قبح هذه الأفعال بقيت الآية حجة في ما ليس بقبيح من أفعال الخلق على أن إيجاد القبيح ليس بقبيح في المعقول، إذ تحصيل الشيء على ما ينبغي أن يكون عليه من حسن وقبح حكمة ، كما أن العلم به على ما هو عليه علم وليس بجهل، ونبين حقيقة هذا الكلام إذا انتهينا إلى المعقول في المسألة - إن شاء الله.
The occurrence of the verse indicates that the inclusion of the acts of creation is not impossible, because making that impossible necessitates equating it with what creeps and crawls, and that removes the meaning of praise for which the verse was brought. Moreover, we ask them for the proof of impossibility. If they say: the proof of its impossibility is that the Creator is wise, so it is not befitting for Him to create the insult of Himself, then we have answered that. And if they make the proof of impossibility the entry of an object of power under the power of two capable beings, then we say: the context of the verse necessitates the negation of impossibility, because if impossibility were established, the meaning of praise would be removed. And we will show that that is not impossible when we begin discussing the rational (al-ma'qūl), God willing. Moreover, establishing the proof of impossibility is upon them, not upon us. And if they make the proof of impossibility the ugliness of these acts, then the verse remains an argument for what is not ugly among the acts of creation, because bringing into existence the ugly is not ugly in the rational (al-ma'qūl), since procuring a thing as it ought to be, of goodness and ugliness, is wisdom, just as knowledge of it as it is, is knowledge and not ignorance. And we will clarify the reality of this statement when we reach the rational (al-ma'qūl) in the issue, God willing.
Source pages p. 866

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection that human acts cannot be created by God because some acts are ugly (e.g., insulting God), and it would be unbecoming of a wise God to create such ugliness. Nasafi begins by citing the verse (presumably 'Allah is the Creator of all things') and argues that if creating acts were impossible, it would equate God's acts with those of mere creatures, removing the praise intended by the verse. He then challenges the opponent to provide evidence for impossibility. If they argue from divine wisdom, he says they have already been answered. If they argue that two capable beings cannot share power over one act, he counters that the verse itself negates impossibility. If they argue from the ugliness of acts, he points out that the verse still covers non-ugly acts, and moreover, creating something ugly is not itself ugly in rational terms because the act of creation is not subject to moral categories in the same way as the created act; rather, wisdom consists in bringing things into existence as they should be. He promises to elaborate further when discussing rational arguments. The argument follows a typical kalam structure: presenting an objection, then refuting it step by step.

Key Terms
أفعال الخلق
الاستحالة
الحكيم
القبيح
المعقول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God cannot create ugly acts because it would be evil for Him to do so.
Correction: The act of creation is not subject to moral judgment; wisdom is in bringing things into existence as they should be, and creating something ugly is not itself ugly.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument Nasafi uses to refute the idea that God cannot create ugly acts?
A) Such acts are not really ugly.
B) The verse 'Allah is the Creator of all things' includes all acts, and creating ugliness is not ugly in rational terms.
C) God only creates good acts.
D) The acts are not truly created by God.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi establishes that the act of creation is not subject to moral ugliness; rather, wisdom governs creation, so God can create any act without compromising His perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own sins or the evil in the world, do you ever secretly think that God could not have created that, as if it tarnishes His perfection? How does Nasafi's distinction between creating an act and the act itself challenge that assumption? Will you now see your failings as ultimately within God's wisdom, even if you don't understand it?
?
You often judge actions as 'ugly' and demand that God distance Himself from them. But have you considered that your sense of ugliness might be limited? If wisdom is bringing about things as they ought to be, are you willing to trust God's wisdom even when you cannot see the 'ought'? What would it take for you to submit to that trust today?
?
Nasafi argues that making human acts impossible for God would equate Him with creatures. Are there areas of your life where you limit God's power by assuming He cannot work through your weaknesses or mistakes? What would change if you truly believed He is the Creator of all your actions, even the ones you regret?

The Three Proofs Against Created Power
The author states the claim and enumerates three proofs with their logical basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational proofs that demonstrate the impossibility of creative power for any being other than Allah.

Core Idea
Allah alone creates; no other can share this power.

Imam Nasafi begins by stating the impossibility of creative power for other than Allah and provides three proofs. The first proof focuses on the condition of knowledge, the second on intellectual testimony, and the third on the impossibility of leading to absurdity. This lesson will outline these three proofs succinctly before delving deeper into the first.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening passage
Read the passage from the beginning to the end of the three proofs. Note the strong language and logical structure.
The author uses the term 'impossible' (muḥāl) repeatedly.
2
Identify the three proofs
The text presents three distinct proofs marked by 'one of them', 'the second', 'the third'. Locate each and summarize their core idea.
The first proof is about a missing condition, the second is intellectual testimony, the third is about leading to absurdity.
3
Reflect on the logical flow
Notice how the third proof uses the principle that the sound does not produce the corrupt. Consider why this is a convincing argument.
This principle is foundational in Kalam.
4
Prepare for deeper study
The next lesson will explore the first proof in detail. For now, ensure you can list all three proofs from memory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى محال: الدليل على ذلك وجوه: أحدها فقد شرط ثبوت تلك القدرة وثبوت الشيء في حال انعدام شرطه الذي علق وجوده به محال تشهد العقول الصحيحة بفطرها بإحالته. والآخر: شهادة نفس العقل. والثالث: أن إثبات قدرة التخليق له يؤدي إلى أمر محال عرفت إحالته بإجماع الخصوم وشهادة العقول وما يؤدي إلى المحال يعرف إحالته لأن الصحيح لا ينتج الفاسد، والحق لا يولد الباطل. [الأول: فقد شرط ثبوت قدرة التخليق للعبد] أما الأول فبيانه أن شرط ثبوت قدرة التخليق هو ثبوت العلم للخالق بالمخلوق قبل حصول المخلوق، ودليل كون ذلك شرطا كتاب الله تعالى ومساعدة الخصوم وشهادات المعارف، أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَسِرُّوا قَوْلَكُمْ أَوِ اجْهَرُوا بِهِ إِنَّهُ عَلِيمٌ بِذَاتِ الصُّدُورِ أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الْخَبِيرُ ﴾ فالآية تنص على أنه خالق أفعال العباد، وفيها أيضًا إشارة إلى أن كل خالق ينبغي أن يكون عالمًا بما خلق، أما كونها نصا فظاهر فإنه تعالى أخبر أنه يعلم ما يسر به العبد في قلبه وما يجهر به وقال: أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وهو بيان أنه هو الخالق لأنه جعل كونه خالقًا مقررا لما أخبر من تعلق علمه به كأنه قال: وهل يتصور أن لا يعلم من خلقه وأبدا ثبته بما هو أظهر منه ولا يرتاب أحد في كون الأفعال معلومة لله تعالى والله تعالى جعل العلم بهذا ثابتاً بثبوت تخليقه له، فكان هذا إخباراً بكونه مخلوقا له ثم بنى لثبوت العلم به على كونه مخلوقا له، ومثل هذا من أظهر ما يستدل به من النصوص. وأما الإشارة فلأنه أثبت علمه بما أسروا أو جهروا بإثبات تخليقه لذلك، ولو جاز التخليق ممن لا علم له بما خلق لم يكن إثبات العلم بإثبات ما يجوز ثبوته بدون العلم حكمة، كمن يقول لآخر: أنا عالم بالفقه والكلام ثم يقول: ألا أعلم أنا ذلك وأنا ابن بزاز؟ أو يقول: وأنا طويل أو قصير أو وأنا عراقي أو حجازي أو يقول: ألا يعلم الفقه ممن هو بطل كَمَيٍّ أو جواد سخي؟ جل الله تعالى أن يثبت علمه بشيء بناء على ما لا يوجب له العلم به، ويجوز تعريه عن العلم فيكون في إثباته سفها مثبتًا الشيء بما لا يجب ثبوته به كالذين يجهلون طرق إثبات الأشياء على منكري ثبوتها، فصح ما ادعينا من ثبوت العلم بالمخلوق شرطًا لثبوت قدرة التخليق أو قرينة لها لا يزيلها بوجه من الوجوه في حال من الأحوال مع ما كانت الآية نصا، في إثبات خلق أفعال العباد، فإذا أثبت الله تعالى قول أهل الحق لكتابه نصا
The proof that creative power is impossible for other than Allah Most High: the proof for that is [in] aspects: one of them: the condition for the existence of that power and the existence of a thing in a state of absence of its condition upon which its existence is dependent is impossible, sound intellects testify by their innate disposition to its impossibility. The second: the testimony of the intellect itself. The third: that affirming creative power for him leads to an impossible matter whose impossibility is known by consensus of the opponents and the testimony of intellects, and what leads to the impossible is known to be impossible because the sound does not produce the corrupt, and the truth does not generate falsehood. [The first: for the condition of affirming creative power for the servant] As for the first, its explanation is that the condition for affirming creative power is the existence of knowledge for the Creator of the created before the existence of the created, and the proof that that is a condition is the Book of Allah Most High, the concurrence of the opponents, and the testimonies of rational cognitions. As for the Book, it is His statement: "And conceal your speech or declare it; indeed, He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Aware?" So the verse explicitly states that He is the Creator of the acts of the servants, and in it there is also an indication that every creator should be knowledgeable of what He created. As for its being an explicit text (naṣṣ), it is apparent, for He Most High informed that He knows what the servant conceals in his heart and what he declares openly, and said: "Does He who created not know?" and it is an explanation that He is the Creator because He made His being Creator a confirmation of what He informed of the relation of His knowledge to it, as if He said: Can it be imagined that He does not know what He created? And He established it by what is more apparent than it, and no one doubts that the acts are known to Allah Most High, and Allah Most High made knowledge of this established by the establishment of His creating it, so this was an announcement of its being created by Him, then He based the establishment of knowledge of it upon its being created by Him, and such is among the most apparent things used as evidence from the texts. As for the indication (ishāra), it is because He established His knowledge of what they concealed or declared openly by establishing His creating it for that, and if creation were permissible from one who has no knowledge of what he created, then establishing knowledge by establishing that which can be established without knowledge would not be wisdom, like one who says to another: I am knowledgeable of jurisprudence and theology, then says: Do I not know that? And I am the son of a vendor? Or he says: And I am tall or short or I am Iraqi or Hijazi, or he says: Does not know jurisprudence one who is a hero like Kumayt or a generous horseman? Far exalted is Allah Most High above establishing His knowledge of something based on what does not necessitate knowledge of it, and [above] allowing its divestment of knowledge, for then in establishing it there would be foolishness, establishing the thing by what does not require its establishment, like those who are ignorant of the methods of establishing things against deniers of their existence. So what we claimed is correct: that the existence of knowledge of the created is a condition for the existence of creative power, or a concomitant that cannot be removed in any way or in any state, especially since the verse is explicit in establishing the creation of the acts of the servants. So Allah Most High established the saying of the people of truth in His Book as an explicit text.
Source pages p. 872

Commentary
This passage is a proof argument demonstrating the impossibility of anyone other than Allah possessing creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq). The author, Imam Nasafi, presents three proofs, then elaborates the first in detail. The passage begins by stating the claim: it is impossible for other than Allah to have creative power. The first proof: a condition for the existence of such power is that the creator must have knowledge of the created before its existence; if the condition is absent, the thing is impossible. Sound intellects testify to this. The second proof: the intellect itself bears witness. The third proof: affirming such power for another leads to an absurdity agreed upon by opponents and intellect; what leads to absurdity is itself impossible because sound premises cannot produce a corrupt conclusion. The author then focuses on the first proof, explaining that the condition is knowledge, citing the Qur'an (Surah al-Mulk 67:13-14) as an explicit text (naṣṣ) and also as an indication (ishāra). The verse explicitly states Allah creates acts and knows them; the indication is that He links knowledge to creation, implying creation cannot occur without knowledge. The author uses analogies to show the absurdity of claiming creation without knowledge, comparing it to someone claiming knowledge while giving irrelevant proofs. He concludes that knowledge of the created is a necessary condition or concomitant for creative power, confirmed by the clear text.

Key Terms
قدرة التخليق
شرط
محال
العقول
فاسد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the three proofs in this passage, which proof explicitly mentions the consensus of opponents?
A) The first proof
B) The second proof
C) The third proof
D) None of them

Key Takeaway
The three proofs together establish that creative power is unique to Allah, using conditions, intellectual testimony, and logical consequence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever credited a human being or a system with the power to truly bring about something from nothing in your life, even in your heart? What does this passage reveal about the subtle shirk in attributing independent causality to anyone besides Allah? Will you commit to consciously reminding yourself daily that all creation is from Allah alone?
?
The third proof teaches that sound premises do not produce corrupt conclusions. Reflect on a time when you accepted a flawed premise about Allah or His attributes – how did that lead you to a wrong belief or action? Are you willing to examine your current beliefs to ensure they are 'sound' (ṣaḥīḥ) as the intellect requires?
?
The first proof says the condition for creative power is absent in anyone but Allah. In your reliance on others (people, wealth, skills), have you ever felt a sense of ultimate control or power in them? How does this lesson call you to shift your trust (tawakkul) entirely to the One who truly possesses creative power? Write down one practical step you will take today to act on this truth.

Knowledge as a Condition for Creative Power
The author elaborates the first proof, using Qur'anic evidence and rational argument to establish knowledge as a condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic verse and rational indication establish knowledge as a necessary condition for creation.

Core Idea
A creator must know what He creates.

In this lesson, we examine the first proof in detail: the condition that a creator must have knowledge of the created before its existence. Imam Nasafi uses both the explicit text (nas) and indicative interpretation (ishara) of the Qur'anic verse to demonstrate this, supported by rational analogy. This deep dive shows how Kalam scholars integrate scripture and reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the detailed elaboration
Read the passage starting from 'As for the first, its explanation is...' to the end. Follow the argument carefully.
The argument has two main parts: the explicit text (naṣṣ) and the indication (ishāra).
2
Understand the explicit text (naṣṣ)
The author cites the verse and explains why it explicitly states that Allah is the Creator of acts and that He knows them. Note how he uses 'does He who created not know?' as a rhetorical question.
The verse is Surah al-Mulk 67:13-14.
3
Analyze the indication (ishāra)
The author argues that the verse links knowledge to creation, implying that creation cannot occur without knowledge. He uses analogies to show the absurdity of claiming creation without knowledge.
The analogies involve someone claiming knowledge based on irrelevant attributes.
4
Synthesize the conclusion
The author concludes that knowledge of the created is a necessary condition or inseparable concomitant for creative power, supported by the explicit text and rational indication.
This refutes the possibility of creation by anyone other than Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى محال: الدليل على ذلك وجوه: أحدها فقد شرط ثبوت تلك القدرة وثبوت الشيء في حال انعدام شرطه الذي علق وجوده به محال تشهد العقول الصحيحة بفطرها بإحالته. والآخر: شهادة نفس العقل. والثالث: أن إثبات قدرة التخليق له يؤدي إلى أمر محال عرفت إحالته بإجماع الخصوم وشهادة العقول وما يؤدي إلى المحال يعرف إحالته لأن الصحيح لا ينتج الفاسد، والحق لا يولد الباطل. [الأول: فقد شرط ثبوت قدرة التخليق للعبد] أما الأول فبيانه أن شرط ثبوت قدرة التخليق هو ثبوت العلم للخالق بالمخلوق قبل حصول المخلوق، ودليل كون ذلك شرطا كتاب الله تعالى ومساعدة الخصوم وشهادات المعارف، أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَسِرُّوا قَوْلَكُمْ أَوِ اجْهَرُوا بِهِ إِنَّهُ عَلِيمٌ بِذَاتِ الصُّدُورِ أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الْخَبِيرُ ﴾ فالآية تنص على أنه خالق أفعال العباد، وفيها أيضًا إشارة إلى أن كل خالق ينبغي أن يكون عالمًا بما خلق، أما كونها نصا فظاهر فإنه تعالى أخبر أنه يعلم ما يسر به العبد في قلبه وما يجهر به وقال: أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وهو بيان أنه هو الخالق لأنه جعل كونه خالقًا مقررا لما أخبر من تعلق علمه به كأنه قال: وهل يتصور أن لا يعلم من خلقه وأبدا ثبته بما هو أظهر منه ولا يرتاب أحد في كون الأفعال معلومة لله تعالى والله تعالى جعل العلم بهذا ثابتاً بثبوت تخليقه له، فكان هذا إخباراً بكونه مخلوقا له ثم بنى لثبوت العلم به على كونه مخلوقا له، ومثل هذا من أظهر ما يستدل به من النصوص. وأما الإشارة فلأنه أثبت علمه بما أسروا أو جهروا بإثبات تخليقه لذلك، ولو جاز التخليق ممن لا علم له بما خلق لم يكن إثبات العلم بإثبات ما يجوز ثبوته بدون العلم حكمة، كمن يقول لآخر: أنا عالم بالفقه والكلام ثم يقول: ألا أعلم أنا ذلك وأنا ابن بزاز؟ أو يقول: وأنا طويل أو قصير أو وأنا عراقي أو حجازي أو يقول: ألا يعلم الفقه ممن هو بطل كَمَيٍّ أو جواد سخي؟ جل الله تعالى أن يثبت علمه بشيء بناء على ما لا يوجب له العلم به، ويجوز تعريه عن العلم فيكون في إثباته سفها مثبتًا الشيء بما لا يجب ثبوته به كالذين يجهلون طرق إثبات الأشياء على منكري ثبوتها، فصح ما ادعينا من ثبوت العلم بالمخلوق شرطًا لثبوت قدرة التخليق أو قرينة لها لا يزيلها بوجه من الوجوه في حال من الأحوال مع ما كانت الآية نصا، في إثبات خلق أفعال العباد، فإذا أثبت الله تعالى قول أهل الحق لكتابه نصا
The proof that creative power is impossible for other than Allah Most High: the proof for that is [in] aspects: one of them: the condition for the existence of that power and the existence of a thing in a state of absence of its condition upon which its existence is dependent is impossible, sound intellects testify by their innate disposition to its impossibility. The second: the testimony of the intellect itself. The third: that affirming creative power for him leads to an impossible matter whose impossibility is known by consensus of the opponents and the testimony of intellects, and what leads to the impossible is known to be impossible because the sound does not produce the corrupt, and the truth does not generate falsehood. [The first: for the condition of affirming creative power for the servant] As for the first, its explanation is that the condition for affirming creative power is the existence of knowledge for the Creator of the created before the existence of the created, and the proof that that is a condition is the Book of Allah Most High, the concurrence of the opponents, and the testimonies of rational cognitions. As for the Book, it is His statement: "And conceal your speech or declare it; indeed, He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Aware?" So the verse explicitly states that He is the Creator of the acts of the servants, and in it there is also an indication that every creator should be knowledgeable of what He created. As for its being an explicit text (naṣṣ), it is apparent, for He Most High informed that He knows what the servant conceals in his heart and what he declares openly, and said: "Does He who created not know?" and it is an explanation that He is the Creator because He made His being Creator a confirmation of what He informed of the relation of His knowledge to it, as if He said: Can it be imagined that He does not know what He created? And He established it by what is more apparent than it, and no one doubts that the acts are known to Allah Most High, and Allah Most High made knowledge of this established by the establishment of His creating it, so this was an announcement of its being created by Him, then He based the establishment of knowledge of it upon its being created by Him, and such is among the most apparent things used as evidence from the texts. As for the indication (ishāra), it is because He established His knowledge of what they concealed or declared openly by establishing His creating it for that, and if creation were permissible from one who has no knowledge of what he created, then establishing knowledge by establishing that which can be established without knowledge would not be wisdom, like one who says to another: I am knowledgeable of jurisprudence and theology, then says: Do I not know that? And I am the son of a vendor? Or he says: And I am tall or short or I am Iraqi or Hijazi, or he says: Does not know jurisprudence one who is a hero like Kumayt or a generous horseman? Far exalted is Allah Most High above establishing His knowledge of something based on what does not necessitate knowledge of it, and [above] allowing its divestment of knowledge, for then in establishing it there would be foolishness, establishing the thing by what does not require its establishment, like those who are ignorant of the methods of establishing things against deniers of their existence. So what we claimed is correct: that the existence of knowledge of the created is a condition for the existence of creative power, or a concomitant that cannot be removed in any way or in any state, especially since the verse is explicit in establishing the creation of the acts of the servants. So Allah Most High established the saying of the people of truth in His Book as an explicit text.
Source pages p. 872

Commentary
This passage is a proof argument demonstrating the impossibility of anyone other than Allah possessing creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq). The author, Imam Nasafi, presents three proofs, then elaborates the first in detail. The passage begins by stating the claim: it is impossible for other than Allah to have creative power. The first proof: a condition for the existence of such power is that the creator must have knowledge of the created before its existence; if the condition is absent, the thing is impossible. Sound intellects testify to this. The second proof: the intellect itself bears witness. The third proof: affirming such power for another leads to an absurdity agreed upon by opponents and intellect; what leads to absurdity is itself impossible because sound premises cannot produce a corrupt conclusion. The author then focuses on the first proof, explaining that the condition is knowledge, citing the Qur'an (Surah al-Mulk 67:13-14) as an explicit text (naṣṣ) and also as an indication (ishāra). The verse explicitly states Allah creates acts and knows them; the indication is that He links knowledge to creation, implying creation cannot occur without knowledge. The author uses analogies to show the absurdity of claiming creation without knowledge, comparing it to someone claiming knowledge while giving irrelevant proofs. He concludes that knowledge of the created is a necessary condition or concomitant for creative power, confirmed by the clear text.

Key Terms

العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the proof is circular: assuming Allah creates to prove knowledge, then using knowledge to prove creation.
Correction: The author uses the Qur'anic verse which explicitly states both creation and knowledge, not as a dependent assumption. The indication argument shows that if creation were possible without knowledge, then using creation to establish knowledge would be logically flawed, so creation necessitates knowledge.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the indication (ishāra) argument in this passage?
A) The verse explicitly states that Allah creates acts.
B) If creation were possible without knowledge, using creation to prove knowledge would be foolish.
C) The opponents agree that creation requires knowledge.
D) The intellect alone testifies to the impossibility.

Key Takeaway
The condition of knowledge for creation is established through both the explicit text of the Qur'an and the logical indication that creation necessitates knowledge, making creative power unique to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's knowledge of your every action is a condition for His creation of that action, what does that mean for how you view the acts you perform today? Are you living as though each moment is known and created by Him? What one habit will you change to remind yourself of this?
?
The author says it would be foolish to claim knowledge based on something that can exist without knowledge. In what areas of your life do you attribute your good deeds to your own ability, forgetting that Allah's knowledge and power are the real source? How can you realign your gratitude today?
?
The verse asks: 'Does He who created not know?' – do you ever act as if Allah does not see you? Think of a moment this week when you acted inconsistently with His knowledge. What will you do differently the next time you are tempted to ignore His awareness?
