intermediate
5 min
Why God Cannot Create Power for an Impossible Act
Imam al-Nasafi proves by analogy that God cannot create power for an act He cannot do.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi proof that it is impossible for God to create power in a creature for an action that God Himself cannot perform, based on the analogy with knowledge.

Core Idea
The creator must possess the attribute He creates; otherwise it's a contradiction.

Imam al-Nasafi presents a powerful analogy to refute the Mu'tazilite position that God can create power in humans for actions God cannot do. He argues that just as it is impossible for God to create knowledge of something He does not know, so too it is impossible for Him to create power over something He is not powerful over. This argument appeals to both logical reasoning and innate human intuition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm and analogy come through.
2
Identify the analogy used
The passage compares power to knowledge. Find how the author draws the parallel and what conclusion follows.
3
Note the appeal to common sense
The author says even common people would reject the Mu'tazilite view. Think about why this appeal strengthens the argument.
Innate intuition (badaha) is considered a reliable source of knowledge in kalam.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The key principle is that the creator must possess the attribute He creates. Reflect on why this is logically necessary.
Otherwise, the creation would involve a contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنه عاجز وهو محال ، وكذا من المحال أن يعلم ذات غيره شيئًا لم يكن ذلك الشيء معلومًا لهذا العلم من غير فصل بين القديم والمحدث، فكذا هذا، وإحالة هذا مما تعرفه العوام ببدائههم وأوائل عقولهم حتى لو صور لأغبى خليقة الله تعالى من العوام قول المعتزلة في تجويز تخليق الله تعالى القدرة للعبد على ما لا يقدر الله تعالى عليه بنفسه أو يقدر أحد من العباد إقدار ذات ما على ما لا يقدر عليه الذات المقدر، لتسارعوا إلى تسفيه القائل له الراضى بذلك مذهبًا لنفسه، كما يعرفون إحالة تعليم ذات ما ذاتاً ما لا علم لا للمعلم به، ويتسارعون إلى تسفيه المجوز لذلك وذلك محال، وخروج عن قضية البداهة وأوائل العقول فكذا هذا، ألا ترى أن القول بتخليق قدرة ممن ليس بقادر عليها محال كما أن القول بتخليق علم ممن ليس بعالم به محال فكذا القول بتخليق قدرة على فعل ممن ليس بقادر على ذلك الفعل يكون محالاً كالقول بتخليق علم بمعلوم ممن ليس بعالم بذلك المعلوم.
It is impossible for Him, and likewise it is impossible that He should know something of another which is not known to this knowledge without distinction between the eternal and the originated. So likewise this. And the impossibility of this is something that the common people know by their innate intuitions and first principles of their intellects, so much so that if the statement of the Mu'tazila were presented to the most obtuse of God's creatures among the common people — concerning their allowing God to create power for the servant over what God Almighty is not powerful over Himself, or that any of the servants could empower a being over what that being is not powerful over — they would hasten to consider foolish the one who says it and is satisfied with that as his doctrine, just as they know the impossibility of teaching a being something that the teacher has no knowledge of, and they hasten to consider foolish the one who permits that. And that is impossible and a departure from the dictate of innate intuition and first principles of intellects. So likewise this. Do you not see that the statement about creating power from one who is not powerful over it is impossible, just as the statement about creating knowledge from one who is not knowing of it is impossible? So likewise the statement about creating power for an act from one who is not powerful over that act would be impossible, like the statement about creating knowledge of a known thing from one who is not knowing of that known thing.
Source pages p. 885

Commentary
This passage is a proof by analogy demonstrating that it is impossible for God to create power in a creature for an action that God Himself is not capable of performing. The author begins by stating that it is impossible for God to be incapable of something, and then draws an analogy with knowledge: just as it is impossible for God to create knowledge of something He does not know, so too it is impossible for Him to create power over something He is not powerful over. He emphasizes that this is intuitive even for common people, so much so that if the Mu'tazilite position were presented to them, they would immediately reject it as foolish. The argument relies on the principle that the creator must possess the attribute He creates, otherwise it would be a logical contradiction.

Key Terms
قدرة (power)
عاجز (incapable)
محال (impossible)
بداهة (innate intuition)
تخليق (creation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God can create power in a creature to do something God cannot do.
Correction: This is impossible because the creator must possess the attribute He creates. If God cannot do an act, He cannot create power for that act.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to prove that God cannot create power for an act He cannot do?
A) The analogy of knowledge: just as God cannot create knowledge of something He does not know.
B) The analogy of will: just as God cannot create will for something He does not will.
C) The analogy of life: just as God cannot create life for something He does not have.
D) The analogy of speech: just as God cannot create speech for something He does not say.

Key Takeaway
God cannot create power for an act He cannot do, just as He cannot create knowledge of something He does not know, because the creator must possess the attribute He creates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's power, do you ever imagine it as something He could 'lend out' or delegate, like a borrowed tool? How does this lesson's insistence that the Creator must possess every attribute He creates challenge that mental picture?
?
If even the most ignorant person recognizes the absurdity of God creating power for an act He cannot do, what does that say about your own intellectual pride when you are tempted to rationalize a view that contradicts clear reason?
?
This lesson uses an analogy between knowledge and power. In your own life, are there areas where you claim to 'know' something but do not 'act' on it? How does the inseparable connection between knowledge and action in God's attributes call you to align your own knowledge with practice?

Refuting the Objection: God Creates Will Without Being Willful
Imam al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite analogy by asserting the generality of God's will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, according to Maturidi doctrine, God cannot create will for an act without willing it, and why the Mu'tazilite analogy with power fails.

Core Idea
God's will is all-encompassing; He cannot create will for something He does not will.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi faces a clever objection from the Mu'tazila. They argue that if God can create will in a person without Himself being willing, He should similarly create power without being powerful. Nasafi's response hinges on the unique scope of God's will, which covers all created things. Let's examine the logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite objection
Read the first sentence of the Arabic passage and its translation. Understand the analogy they propose: just as God creates will for an act without being willing, He should be able to create power without being powerful.
2
Examine Nasafi's refutation
Read the rest of the passage. Nasafi denies the analogy, stating that God's will is general over all created things, making it impossible for Him to create a will for something He does not will.
The key difference between will and power is that God's will is all-encompassing, while power is not necessarily so in the same way.
3
Understand the underlying principle
Reflect on the Maturidi principle of 'عموم الإرادة' (generality of will). This doctrine means that God wills every created thing, so creating a will for a creature for an act implies that God wills that act as well.
This refutation shows that the Mu'tazilite objection is based on a misunderstanding of God's will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: لما جاز أن يخلق الباري جل جلاله إرادة الفعل لا يكون هذا مريدًا له، فلم لا يجوز أن يخلق قدرة على فعل لا قدرة له عليه؟ قيل: عندنا لا فرق بين هذا وبين ما ألزمنا، فإن الله تعالى كما يستحيل أن يخلق قدرة لغيره على فعل لا قدرة له على ذلك الفعل يستحيل أن يخلق إرادة لغيره لفعل لا يكون هو مريدًا لذلك الفعل لما نبين بعد هذا أن من مذهبنا القول بعموم إرادة الله تعالى المحدثات، وهذا السؤال بنيتم على أصلكم الفاسد.
If they say: When it is permissible for the Exalted Creator to create will for an act without Him being willing of it, why is it not permissible for Him to create power over an act without being powerful over it? It is said: According to us, there is no difference between this and what we have imposed. For God, just as it is impossible for Him to create power for another over an act without being powerful over that act, it is impossible for Him to create will for another for an act without being willing of that act, because we will explain later that our doctrine holds the generality of God's will over originated things. And this question is based on your corrupt principle.
Source pages p. 885

Commentary
This passage presents a Mu'tazilite objection and the author's response. The objectors argue that since God can create will in a person for an action without Himself being willing of that action, He should also be able to create power in a person for an action without Himself being powerful over it. The author refutes by stating that according to his school (Maturidi doctrine), there is no such distinction: God's will is general over all created things, so it is impossible for Him to create a will for something He does not will. The difference between will and power is that God's will is all-encompassing, so the analogy does not hold.

Key Terms
إرادة (will)
قدرة (power)
مريد (willing)
قادر (powerful)
عموم الإرادة (generality of will)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that creating a will in a creature for an act does not require the creator to will that act, analogous to creating power.
Correction: According to Maturidi doctrine, God's will is all-encompassing (عموم الإرادة), so it is impossible for Him to create a will for something He does not will. The analogy with power does not hold because will and power function differently with respect to God.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why can't God create will for an act without being willing of it?
A) Because God's will is general over all created things.
B) Because God cannot create anything.
C) Because will is not an attribute.
D) Because the Mu'tazila are wrong.

Key Takeaway
God's will is all-encompassing, so He cannot create a will for an act without willing it — a key Maturidi principle refuting the Mu'tazilite analogy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does this lesson affect your view of your own intentions? Commit to repeating 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' daily to reaffirm that all will and power belong to Him.
?
If God's will encompasses all, then your good and bad intentions are created by Him. How does this make you feel about your responsibility? Does it lead you to rely more on Him or to despair? Today, ask God to purify your intentions and make you aware that even your turning to Him is by His will.
?
The Mu'tazilites denied the generality of God's will because they found it uncomfortable. Are there aspects of God's decree that you find hard to accept? Will you surrender to His will even when it conflicts with your own reasoning? Pray for the ability to accept His qadr fully.

Refuting the Claim that God's Will Can Embrace Contraries
Imam al-Nasafi answers the objection that creating wills for contrary acts would imply God wills impossible things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that God's creating wills for contrary acts leads to willing impossibilities is invalid, and how the distinction between will (irāda) and wish (tamannī) resolves it.

Core Idea
God's will is always effective; without an act, it is merely a wish.

Imam al-Nasafi addresses a key objection: if God creates wills for opposite actions in different people, wouldn't He be willing contradictory things? This would be impossible. The answer lies in a critical distinction: a will that does not result in the act is not truly will—it is a wish. Since God's will is always fulfilled, there is no contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objectors claim that if God creates wills for contrary acts in different loci at the same time, then God wills both contraries, which is impossible.
Note the structure of the objection: it assumes that any created will implies God's will for that act.
2
Find the answer's key move
The author immediately calls the objection deceptive or ignorant. Then he provides the core distinction: a will without a corresponding act is not a true will but a wish.
The decisive point: God only creates will for acts that actually occur.
3
Understand the implication
Since God is all-powerful, His will is always effective. So He cannot create a will for an act that does not happen. Thus, the scenario of two contrary created wills both being true wills cannot occur.
This refutes the objection without denying God's power.
4
Review the distinction between will and wish
The passage defines true will as accompanied by the act; otherwise it is wish. This is a key principle in Maturidi theology.
This distinction will be elaborated later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: القول بما قلتم يؤدي إلى أن يوجد من الله تعالى إرادة للمتضادين في محل واحد في وقت واحد، فإنه إذا خلق لذات ما إرادة لفعل في محل، وخلق لآخر إرادة ضد ذلك الفعل في عين ذلك المحل في تلك الساعة، وكان هو تعالى مريدًا ما خلق لكل واحد منهما إرادته من الفعل كان مؤديا إلى ذلك وهو محال. قيل: هذا السؤال تمويه منكم إن عرفتم حقيقة الإرادة وإلا فهو صادر عن الجهل بحقيقتها، وهذا لأن تخليق الإرادة لذاتين لفعلين متضادين في وقت واحد في محل واحد محال كتخليق فعلين، فإن الإرادة بدون الفعل محال وكل ما يظن إرادة إذا لم يطابقه الفعل ولم يقترن به فهو تمن وليس بإرادة فلا يكون كل واحد منهما إرادة بل ما قارنه الفعل فهو إرادة لم يقارنه الفعل فهو تَمَنِّ على ما نبين حقيقة هذا إذا انتهينا إلى مسألة الإرادة إن شاء الله تعالى.
If they say: The statement you have made leads to the existence from God of will for two contraries in one locus at one time. For if He creates for a being a will for an act in a locus, and creates for another a will for the contrary of that act in the same locus at that moment, and He is willing of what He created for each of them of will for the act, then that would lead to that, which is impossible. It is said: This question is a deception from you if you know the reality of will; otherwise it arises from ignorance of its reality. This is because the creation of will for two beings for two contrary acts at one time in one locus is impossible, like the creation of two acts. For will without an act is impossible. And everything that is thought to be will if the act does not correspond to it and is not accompanied by it, then it is a wish (tamannī) and not a will. So each of them is not a will, but rather that which the act accompanies is will; that which the act does not accompany is a wish, as we will explain the reality of this when we reach the question of will, God willing.
Source pages p. 885

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection that the previous position (that God creates will in a creature only if He wills the corresponding act) would lead to God willing contraries simultaneously if He creates wills for contrary acts in different people. The author responds by distinguishing between true will (irāda) and wish (tamannī). True will must be accompanied by the act; if the act does not occur, it is merely a wish. Since God is all-powerful, His will always results in the act, so He cannot create a will for an act that does not occur. Therefore, there is no contradiction because God wills each act individually, and the creation of a will for a contrary act does not imply He wills it if the act does not follow.

Key Terms
إرادة
تمني
فعل
محل
متضادين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God could will two logically contradictory things at the same time because He is omnipotent.
Correction: God's will is always effective; thus He cannot will an act that does not occur. The scenario of contrary wills cannot arise because one of them would not be a true will.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes a true will from a mere wish according to the author?
A) The occurrence of the act.
B) The strength of the desire.
C) The locus of the will.
D) The intention of the person.

Key Takeaway
God's will is always accompanied by its act; a will without an act is merely a wish, removing any contradiction of omnipotence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Wish vs. Will: The Disanalogy with Power
Imam al-Nasafi explains why creating a wish in a creature is not analogous to creating power for an act God cannot do.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why creating a wish in a creature does not imply that God can create power over acts He cannot do, and how wish differs from will.

Core Idea
Wish does not require action; God's will always does.

Imam al-Nasafi answers a final objection: if God can create a wish for an act without wishing it, why can't He create power without being powerful? The key is that wish, unlike will, does not require the act to occur. Let's see how the argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection carefully: the opponents draw a parallel between wish and power. If God can create wish without being a wisher, why can't He create power without being powerful?
Notice the parallel they try to establish.
2
Distinguish wish from will
The answer begins by highlighting that wish is distinct from will because a wish can exist even if the act does not occur, but God's will is always effective.
This is the core distinction.
3
Analyze the two scenarios
The passage then considers two cases: if the act exists, the servant's will and God's will coincide; if the act does not exist, the servant has wish (not will) and God wills non-existence.
This shows God is never in the position of having wish.
4
Conclude the disanalogy
Since power over an act requires the creator to have that power, but wish does not require the creator to be a wisher, the analogy fails. Creating power without having it is impossible.
The passage ends with 'and in the case of wish, it is otherwise.'
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why this argument is important for understanding God's attributes. It clarifies that divine power is not analogous to human wish in terms of creation.
This connects to the broader theme of divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: لما جاز أن يخلق الله التمني لفعل لا يكون متمنيًا لذلك الفعل لماذا لا يجوز أن يخلق قدرة على فعل لا يكون هو قادرا على ذلك الفعل؟ قيل: هذا السؤال فاسد لما مر أن التمني يمتاز عن الإرادة بوجود مفارقة الفعل إياه وعدم المفارقة، ولا يجوز أن لا يوجد ما يريده الله تعالى فلا يتصور منه التمني، فإن كان ذلك الفعل مما يوجد فما وجد من العبد إرادة وتعلقت به أيضا إرادة الله تعالى وإن كان ذلك الفعل مما لا يوجد فما حصل من العبد تَمَنْ لا إرادة والله تعالى كان مريدًا عدم ذلك الفعل لا وجوده فبعدم ذلك الفعل الذي يريد عدمه لا يكون متمنيًا بل يكون مريدًا عدمه، ألا ترى أنه لا يكون متمنيًا للتمني الذي خلقه فلا يكون متمنيًا للفعل الذي خلق له التمني، فأما فيما نحن فيه فيستحيل أن يخلق قدرة لا قدرة له عليها، فيستحيل أن يخلق قدرة على فعل لا قدرة له عليه، وفي التمني بخلافه والله الموفق.
If they say: When it is permissible for God to create wish (tamannī) for an act without being a wisher (mutamannī) of that act, why is it not permissible for Him to create power over an act without being powerful over that act? It is said: This question is corrupt because it has passed that wish is distinguished from will by the occurrence of separation of the act from it and non-separation. And it is not permissible that what God wills should not exist, so it is not conceivable that He should have wish. For if that act is something that exists, then from the servant there is will and God's will is also attached to it; and if that act is something that does not exist, then from the servant there is wish, not will, and God is willing of the non-existence of that act, not its existence. So by the non-existence of that act which He wills non-existence, He is not a wisher but rather is willing its non-existence. Do you not see that He is not a wisher of the wish which He created, so He is not a wisher of the act for which He created the wish? As for the case under discussion, it is impossible for Him to create power without being powerful over it; so it is impossible for Him to create power over an act without being powerful over it. And in the case of wish, it is otherwise. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 885

Commentary
This passage addresses a final objection: if God can create a wish (tamannī) in a person without Himself wishing that act, why can He not create power in a person without being powerful over that act? The author argues that wish is distinct from will because a wish does not require the occurrence of the act; it can exist without the act. However, God's will is always effective—whatever He wills must exist. Therefore, it is impossible for God to have a wish, because a wish implies something that may not happen. God either wills the existence of an act (in which case it occurs) or wills its non-existence (in which case it does not occur). So if He creates a wish in a creature for something that does not occur, He is not wishing that thing; He is willing its non-existence. Thus, the analogy fails because power over an act requires the creator to be powerful over it, whereas wish does not require the creator to be a wisher of the act.

Key Terms
تمني (wish)
إرادة (will)
قدرة (power)
متمني (wisher)
فعل (act)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Creating a wish in a creature for an act without being a wisher is analogous to creating power in a creature for an act without being powerful over it.
Correction: Wish does not require the act to occur, so the analogy fails because power over an act requires the creator to be powerful over it.

Checkpoint
Why can God create a wish in a creature for an act without being a wisher of that act?
A) Because wish does not require the act to occur.
B) Because wish is the same as will.
C) Because God cannot create wishes.
D) Because wishes are not real.

Key Takeaway
God can create wish without being a wisher, but He cannot create power without being powerful, because wish does not entail the act while power does.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Nullifying Tawhid by Justice and Justice by Tawhid
First two contradictions of Mu'tazila between justice and tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila's attempts to uphold justice and tawhid lead to contradictory outcomes that undermine both principles.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila's justice nullifies tawhid, and their tawhid nullifies justice.

This passage reveals a powerful internal critique of Mu'tazilite theology. The author shows that their very efforts to defend divine justice and tawhid end up destroying each other. We will examine the first two contradictions: how affirming a power of creation for others compromises tawhid, and how denying divine attributes makes justice impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Note the two claims: (1) affirming creation power for others nullifies tawhid; (2) denying attributes nullifies justice.
Notice the author's parallel structure.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila motives
Ask why the Mu'tazila made these moves. They wanted to avoid attributing evil acts to God and to preserve His unity.
Their intention was to defend God's justice and oneness.
3
Trace the logical consequences
See how each move backfires: if God does not create acts, partners are needed (nullifying tawhid). If God has no attributes, commands vanish and punishment is arbitrary (nullifying justice).
4
Reflect on the inversion
The phrase 'nullified by this justice' and 'nullified by their tawhid' shows the paradox. Their defense of one principle destroys the other.
This is a classic refutation strategy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المعتزلة إنما يثبتون لغير الله تعالى قدرة التخليق لئلا يكون الله تعالى معاقبًا عباده على ما يخلق هو بنفسه ويخرجه من العدم إلى الوجود، فيكون عادلاً في تعذيبهم غير ظالم في عقابهم، فأبطلوا التوحيد بهذا العدل، وقد بينا أنهم حيث أنكروا أن يكون الكلام معنى قائمًا بذات الله تعالى أو شيء من الصفات بل قالوا بذات لا صفة له تحقيقا للتوحيد فأبطلوا أمره ونهيه وبطل بذلك الحل والحرمة وخرج الفعل عن كونه طاعة أو معصية، وكان التعذيب على ما ليس بمعصية ظلمًا فأبطلوا عدلهم بتوحيدهم، وهذا معنى قول أصحابنا إن المعتزلة أبطلوا عدلهم بتوحيدهم وتوحيدهم بعدلهم، ولو قيل: إنهم أبطلوا عدلهم بعدلهم وتوحيدهم بتوحيدهم لكان صوابًا، وبيانه أنهم أثبتوا الاستطاعة سابقة على الفعل لئلا يؤدي إلى تكليف ما لا يطاق، ثم قررنا أنها تنعدم عند الفعل فإذا كان فعل عندهم لا قدرة للفاعل عليه، وما لا قدرة للفاعل عليه كان تكليفه تكليف ما لا يطاق، والأمر به والنهي عنه باطل والتعذيب عليه ظلم فأبطلوا عدلهم بعدلهم، وأبطلوا توحيدهم بتوحيدهم، فإنه لو جاز وجود العالم بذات لا حياة له ولا قدرة ولا علم ولا سمع ولا بصر لجاز وجود كل جزء من أجزاء العالم بكل جماد وموات، ولم يبق دليل على وجوده بالله تعالى، وصار كل موات وجماد جائز الألوهية ممكن الربوبية.
Then the Mu'tazila affirm for other than Allah a power of creation (qudrat al-takhlīq) in order that Allah not be punishing His servants for what He Himself creates and brings from non-existence into existence, so that He would be just in their torment, not unjust in their punishment. So they nullified tawḥīd by this justice. And we have shown that when they denied that speech (al-kalām) is a meaning subsisting in the essence of Allah or any of the attributes, but rather said an essence without attributes, in pursuit of tawḥīd, they nullified His command and prohibition, and thereby the lawful and forbidden were nullified, and the act ceased to be obedience or disobedience. And torment for what is not disobedience would be injustice, so they nullified their justice by their tawḥīd. This is the meaning of the statement of our companions: 'The Mu'tazila nullified their justice by their tawḥīd and their tawḥīd by their justice.' And if it were said: 'They nullified their justice by their justice and their tawḥīd by their tawḥīd,' it would be correct. Its explanation is that they affirmed capability (al-istiṭā'a) precedent to the act so that it not lead to a burden beyond capacity (taklīf mā lā yuṭāq). Then we established that it ceases at the act. So if, according to them, an act occurs with no power in the agent, and what the agent has no power over is a burden beyond capacity, then commanding and forbidding it is invalid, and torment for it is injustice. So they nullified their justice by their justice, and they nullified their tawḥīd by their tawḥīd. For if it were permissible for the world to exist by an essence with no life, no power, no knowledge, no hearing, no sight, then it would be permissible for every part of the world to exist by every inanimate and dead thing, and there would remain no proof of its existence by Allah, and every dead and inanimate thing would be a possible object of divinity and a possible object of lordship.
Source pages p. 888

Commentary
This passage is a sophisticated refutation of the Mu'tazila's attempt to reconcile divine justice and tawḥīd. The author shows that their efforts are self-defeating. First, they affirm a power of creation for others to avoid God punishing for His own acts—thus they 'nullify tawḥīd by their justice.' Second, they deny that God has attributes (like speech) in order to preserve tawḥīd, but this invalidates divine commands and prohibitions, making any punishment unjust—thus they 'nullify their justice by their tawḥīd.' The author then shows a further contradiction: they affirm that human capability (istiṭā'a) precedes the act to avoid an impossible burden, but then they claim that capability ceases at the moment of the act, so the act occurs without power, which again is an impossible burden and makes punishment unjust—thus 'they nullify their justice by their justice.' Finally, by denying attributes, they allow the possibility that the world exists by an essence without life, knowledge, etc., which would permit any inanimate object to be a creator, destroying the proof for God's existence—thus 'they nullify their tawḥīd by their tawḥīd.'

Key Terms
قدرة التخليق
عدل
توحيد
كلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that affirming human power or denying attributes separately upholds justice and tawhid.
Correction: This passage shows that these moves are interconnected and each one undermines the other principle.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the Mu'tazila affirm a power of creation for others?
A) To avoid God punishing for His own acts
B) To prove God's power
C) To deny human free will
D) To affirm attributes

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's doctrine of justice undermines tawhid, and their doctrine of tawhid undermines justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself trying to reconcile God's justice with His oneness by reducing one to fit your own logic, like the Mu'tazila did? What would it cost you to accept both fully without compromise?
?
When you think about God's commands, do you ever feel they are arbitrary or just cultural? The Mu'tazila's denial of attributes led to nullifying all commands. Where in your life have you stripped God of His sovereignty to make faith more comfortable?
?
If your own reasoning about God leads to contradictions, are you willing to submit to revelation even when it doesn't 'make sense' to you? What one step will you take today to trust God's consistency over your own?

Nullifying Justice by Justice and Tawhid by Tawhid
Second set of Mu'tazila self-contradictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila's own principles of capability and attribute-denial lead to further contradictions that cancel themselves out.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila's justice nullifies their justice, and their tawhid nullifies their tawhid.

The author continues his critique by showing that even on their own terms, the Mu'tazila cannot escape inconsistency. Their concept of human capability (istiṭā'a) paradoxically makes acts impossible, and their denial of attributes makes creation possible without a Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the two self-nullifications: 'justice by justice' and 'tawhid by tawhid'.
The author first summarizes the previous point, then introduces the new ones.
2
Understand the capability argument
Mu'tazila affirm capability (istiṭā'a) before the act to avoid an impossible burden. But they also hold that capability ceases at the act. So the act occurs without capability, which is itself an impossible burden, making punishment unjust. Thus justice nullifies justice.
Note the double move.
3
Understand the attribute argument
If God can exist without attributes, then any inanimate object could be a creator, removing the proof for God and making tawhid meaningless. Thus tawhid nullifies tawhid.
4
See the pattern
Each doctrine is turned against itself. The very principles they champion produce their own negation.
This is a powerful internal critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المعتزلة إنما يثبتون لغير الله تعالى قدرة التخليق لئلا يكون الله تعالى معاقبًا عباده على ما يخلق هو بنفسه ويخرجه من العدم إلى الوجود، فيكون عادلاً في تعذيبهم غير ظالم في عقابهم، فأبطلوا التوحيد بهذا العدل، وقد بينا أنهم حيث أنكروا أن يكون الكلام معنى قائمًا بذات الله تعالى أو شيء من الصفات بل قالوا بذات لا صفة له تحقيقا للتوحيد فأبطلوا أمره ونهيه وبطل بذلك الحل والحرمة وخرج الفعل عن كونه طاعة أو معصية، وكان التعذيب على ما ليس بمعصية ظلمًا فأبطلوا عدلهم بتوحيدهم، وهذا معنى قول أصحابنا إن المعتزلة أبطلوا عدلهم بتوحيدهم وتوحيدهم بعدلهم، ولو قيل: إنهم أبطلوا عدلهم بعدلهم وتوحيدهم بتوحيدهم لكان صوابًا، وبيانه أنهم أثبتوا الاستطاعة سابقة على الفعل لئلا يؤدي إلى تكليف ما لا يطاق، ثم قررنا أنها تنعدم عند الفعل فإذا كان فعل عندهم لا قدرة للفاعل عليه، وما لا قدرة للفاعل عليه كان تكليفه تكليف ما لا يطاق، والأمر به والنهي عنه باطل والتعذيب عليه ظلم فأبطلوا عدلهم بعدلهم، وأبطلوا توحيدهم بتوحيدهم، فإنه لو جاز وجود العالم بذات لا حياة له ولا قدرة ولا علم ولا سمع ولا بصر لجاز وجود كل جزء من أجزاء العالم بكل جماد وموات، ولم يبق دليل على وجوده بالله تعالى، وصار كل موات وجماد جائز الألوهية ممكن الربوبية.
Then the Mu'tazila affirm for other than Allah a power of creation (qudrat al-takhlīq) in order that Allah not be punishing His servants for what He Himself creates and brings from non-existence into existence, so that He would be just in their torment, not unjust in their punishment. So they nullified tawḥīd by this justice. And we have shown that when they denied that speech (al-kalām) is a meaning subsisting in the essence of Allah or any of the attributes, but rather said an essence without attributes, in pursuit of tawḥīd, they nullified His command and prohibition, and thereby the lawful and forbidden were nullified, and the act ceased to be obedience or disobedience. And torment for what is not disobedience would be injustice, so they nullified their justice by their tawḥīd. This is the meaning of the statement of our companions: 'The Mu'tazila nullified their justice by their tawḥīd and their tawḥīd by their justice.' And if it were said: 'They nullified their justice by their justice and their tawḥīd by their tawḥīd,' it would be correct. Its explanation is that they affirmed capability (al-istiṭā'a) precedent to the act so that it not lead to a burden beyond capacity (taklīf mā lā yuṭāq). Then we established that it ceases at the act. So if, according to them, an act occurs with no power in the agent, and what the agent has no power over is a burden beyond capacity, then commanding and forbidding it is invalid, and torment for it is injustice. So they nullified their justice by their justice, and they nullified their tawḥīd by their tawḥīd. For if it were permissible for the world to exist by an essence with no life, no power, no knowledge, no hearing, no sight, then it would be permissible for every part of the world to exist by every inanimate and dead thing, and there would remain no proof of its existence by Allah, and every dead and inanimate thing would be a possible object of divinity and a possible object of lordship.
Source pages p. 888

Commentary
This passage is a sophisticated refutation of the Mu'tazila's attempt to reconcile divine justice and tawḥīd. The author shows that their efforts are self-defeating. First, they affirm a power of creation for others to avoid God punishing for His own acts—thus they 'nullify tawḥīd by their justice.' Second, they deny that God has attributes (like speech) in order to preserve tawḥīd, but this invalidates divine commands and prohibitions, making any punishment unjust—thus they 'nullify their justice by their tawḥīd.' The author then shows a further contradiction: they affirm that human capability (istiṭā'a) precedes the act to avoid an impossible burden, but then they claim that capability ceases at the moment of the act, so the act occurs without power, which again is an impossible burden and makes punishment unjust—thus 'they nullify their justice by their justice.' Finally, by denying attributes, they allow the possibility that the world exists by an essence without life, knowledge, etc., which would permit any inanimate object to be a creator, destroying the proof for God's existence—thus 'they nullify their tawḥīd by their tawḥīd.'

Key Terms

تكليف ما لا يطاق
عدل
توحيد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that affirming capability before the act solves the problem of impossible burden.
Correction: The author shows that because capability ceases at the act, the act still occurs without capability, making it an impossible burden again.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is one way the Mu'tazila 'nullify their justice by their justice'?
A) By affirming that God creates all actions
B) By affirming capability before the act that ceases at the act
C) By denying the attributes of God
D) By affirming a power of creation for others

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's own doctrines of capability and attribute-denial lead to self-contradiction, nullifying both justice and tawhid from within.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Mu'tazila's denial of attributes leads to the possibility that any inanimate object could be God, then what about your own heart? Have you ever, even implicitly, stripped Allah of His attributes in your mind, making Him less than He is? What specific attribute do you need to affirm more deeply today, and what will you do to remind yourself of it?
?
The Mu'tazila's justice nullifies itself because they set conditions that cannot hold. How about your own sense of justice? Do you hold others to standards that you yourself cannot meet? Will you repent from hypocrisy and ask Allah for true justice in your dealings starting today?
?
The proof for Allah's existence depends on His attributes. If you neglect reflecting on His names and attributes, does your tawhid become hollow? Write down one attribute you will meditate on this week and how it should change your worship, then commit to acting on it.

Two Corruptions from Ma'mar's View on Accidents
Al-Nasafi refutes Ma'mar's doctrine by highlighting two corrupt consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ma'mar's view that bodies create accidents leads to absurd consequences, specifically invalidating divine attributes and implying partners in creation.

Core Idea
Precise acts require a knowing, powerful agent—inanimate objects cannot create accidents.

Ma'mar, a Mu'tazilite leader, claimed that God creates only substances while accidents are produced by bodies themselves. Imam al-Nasafi refutes this by showing it leads to two impossible results: denying God's attributes and making partners with Him. This passage exposes the logical corruption in Ma'mar's view.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without analyzing, then read the translation. Notice the clear structure: statement of Ma'mar's view, then two corruptions introduced by 'أحدها' and 'الآخر'.
The passage ends mid-sentence with 'بوجوه:' indicating a third point that is cut off here.
2
Identify the two corruptions
Locate the two numbered corruptions (أحدها... والآخر...). Understand what each one is arguing against Ma'mar's position.
The first corruption attacks the possibility of accidents coming from inanimate objects; the second attacks the implication of multiple creators.
3
Reflect on the first corruption
Consider why a precise, perfected act must come from an agent with life, knowledge, and power. Why is it absurd to say that inanimate bodies can produce such acts?
This ties directly to the doctrine of divine attributes as necessary for creation.
4
Reflect on the second corruption
Think about the problem of multiple creators. If God only creates substances and bodies create accidents, then the world is jointly created. How does this compare to the dualism of the Magians?
The author says Ma'mar's statement is worse than that of the Magians, though the specific reasons are cut off.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قلنا: إنه يؤدي إلى القول بصانعين، وذلك لأن العالم أعراض وأعيان والله تعالى خالق الأعيان، فأما الأعراض فعلى قول معمر رئيس المعتزلة: لا قدرة الله تعالى على شيء من الأعراض وما تولى هو خلقها ولا إيجادها ولا داخلة تحت قدرته، إنما الأجسام هي التي تخلق الأعراض بعضها بطباعها وبعضها بالاختيار، فما خلق الله تعالى عنده لا صحة ولا سقما ولا موتا ولا حياة ولا لونا ولا رائحة ولا طعماً ولا هيئة ولا تركيبا ولا تأليفًا ولا حركة ولا سكونًا، وغير ذلك وفيه فساد من وجوه: أحدها: أنه جوز تخليق الأعراض من الموات والجمادات ولا حياة لها ولا قدرة ولا علم، وتلك الأعراض أفعال محكمة متقنة وتجويز تخليقها ممن لا علم له ولا قدرة ولا حياة يبطل كون الصانع موصوفا بهذه الصفات، إذ الفعل المحكم المتقن دليل ثبوت هذه الصفات، ولا بداهة للعقول تحكم عليه بالجهل والحمق حيث جوز الأفعال المحكمة ممن لا حياة له ولا علم ولا قدرة. والآخر أنه جعل الله تعالى شركاء في تخليق العالم إذ العالم لما كان منقسما ولم يكن منه إلا قسم واحد، وكان القسم الآخر حاصلاً بغيره كان العالم مخلوقا له ولغيره، ثم كان قوله شرًا من قول المجوس بوجوه:
And we only said: It leads to the statement of two creators. That is because the world consists of accidents (a'rāḍ) and substances (a'yān), and Allah is the Creator of substances. As for accidents, according to the statement of Ma'mar, the chief of the Mu'tazila: Allah has no power over any of the accidents, and He did not undertake their creation nor their bringing into existence, nor are they within His power. Rather, bodies (al-ajsām) are what create the accidents, some by their natures and some by choice. So according to him, Allah did not create health, sickness, death, life, color, odor, taste, shape, composition, combination, motion, rest, or other things. In this there is corruption from several aspects: One of them: That he permitted the creation of accidents from dead and inanimate things which have no life, power, or knowledge. Yet those accidents are precise, perfected acts. Permitting their creation from one who has no knowledge, power, or life invalidates the Creator being described with these attributes, since the precise, perfected act is a proof of the establishment of these attributes. And the primary intellects (badāhat al-'uqūl) would judge him as ignorant and foolish for permitting precise acts from one who has no life, knowledge, or power. Another aspect: That he made Allah have partners in the creation of the world. Since the world is divided and only one part is from Him, while the other part is obtained from others, the world would be created by Him and by others. Then his statement is worse than the statement of the Magians in several respects:
Source pages p. 889

Commentary
This passage refutes Ma'mar's specific doctrine that God creates only substances (a'yān), while accidents (a'rāḍ) are created by bodies (ajsām) either naturally or by choice. The author first states that this leads to the claim of two creators. He then explains Ma'mar's view: God has no power over accidents and did not create them. The author points out two aspects of corruption in this view. First, it permits precise, perfected acts (accidents) to be produced by inanimate objects that lack life, power, and knowledge. This is absurd because a precise act necessarily indicates an agent with those attributes; to claim otherwise is irrational. Second, it makes God a partner in creation, since only substances are from Him while accidents are from bodies, thus the world is jointly created. The author adds that this is worse than the dualism of the Magians (Zoroastrians), but the text cuts off before listing the respects.

معمر
أعراض
أعيان
تخليق الأعراض
المجوس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Accidents can be caused by inanimate objects or bodies without a conscious agent.
Correction: This passage shows that accidents are precise, perfected acts that necessarily require an agent with life, knowledge, and power. Inanimate bodies lack these, so they cannot be the true creators of accidents.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is one consequence of Ma'mar's view that bodies create accidents?
A) It emphasizes God's omnipotence over all things
B) It makes God have partners in creation
C) It eliminates the need for divine attributes
D) It aligns with the Magian view

Key Takeaway
Ma'mar's view that bodies create accidents is false because it implies that precise acts can come from non-living agents, contradicting the necessary attributes of the Creator, and makes God a partner in creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the intricate order of your own body—the beating of your heart, the coordination of your limbs—do you truly realize that every single movement and state is a 'precise, perfected act' created directly by Allah? Or do you subconsciously attribute some of these to mere biological processes, as if they 'just happen'? What would it take for you to see every breath as a direct act of the Creator?
?
Ma'mar's error was to allow that some things in the world come from other than Allah. In your daily life, what 'accidents' of success, provision, or health do you instinctively attribute to your own effort, skill, or luck rather than to Allah's sole creation? How would your gratitude and reliance (tawakkul) change if you truly internalized that not a single accident occurs except by His direct power?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
8 min
Mu'tazilite View Leads to Divine Power Being Created
Logical demonstration that Mu'tazilite position forces divine power into an attribute of action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazilite criterion for distinguishing attributes of self from attributes of action forces them to conclude that divine power is created, a position they themselves reject as kufr.

Core Idea
Mu'tazilite logic undermines their own doctrine by making God's power temporal.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi presents a devastating logical critique of the Mu'tazilite position on divine attributes. The author shows that their own carefully crafted distinction between eternal attributes of God's essence and temporal attributes of action, when applied consistently to the attribute of power (qudra), leads to an unacceptable conclusion: that God's power itself is created and temporal. This not only contradicts their own claim that power is an attribute of the essence, but also forces them into a series of hopeless contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Examine the Mu'tazilite criterion
Read the first part of the passage where the author states the Mu'tazilite rule: an attribute that is always affirmed (never negated) is from the self; one that is sometimes negated is from action. Identify why they put speech (kalam) in the latter category.
The criterion is about affirmation and negation in temporal contexts.
2
Apply the criterion to divine power
See how the author applies the same logic to power: since Mu'tazilites affirm God's power over His own acts but deny it over creatures' acts, power fits the 'affirmed and negated' pattern.
This makes power an attribute of action, hence created (muhdath).
3
Understand the trilemma
The author presents three possible responses the Mu'tazilite might take. Trace each option and note why it leads to contradiction or abandonment of their original position.
Each horn of the trilemma is explained in the passage.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Read the final sentences about falsehood contradicting itself and truth supporting itself. Consider how this principle applies to the argument you have just studied.
The conclusion is a general theological principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قلنا: إن مذهبهم يؤدي إلى القول بكون قدرته من صفات الفعل، وذلك لأن من مذهبهم أن ما يثبت ولا ينفى فهو من صفات الذات، وما يثبت وينفى فهو من صفات الفعل، ولهذا جعلوا الكلام من صفات الفعل، وحكموا بكونه محدثًا لما أنه يثبت وينفي فيقال : إنه كلم موسى عليه السلام ولم يكلم فرعون، فكذا هاهنا يقال إنه يقدر على أفعال نفسه ولا يقدر على أفعال خلقه، فتكون القدرة على قضية قولهم من صفات الفعل فيكون حادثًا، والقول بذلك كفر. فإن زعموا أنه حادث تركوا قولهم: إنه من صفات الذات وهو قادر بنفسه وإن زعموا أنه ليس بحادث وليس من صفات الفعل بل هو من صفات الذات وهو كان موصوفا به في الأزل، فقد زعموا أن قدرته شاملة على المقدورات أجمع وقد أبطلوا قولهم: إنه لا يقدر على أفعال خلقه ورجعوا عن هذه المسألة. وإن تمسكوا بهذه المسألة وتقروا على قولهم: إن القدرة من صفات الذات، فقد أبطلوا على أنفسهم فرقهم بين صفة الذات وصفة الفعل بما ذكروا من الفرق، وإن تمسكوا بكل ذلك فقد ناقضوا أفحش مناقضة، والباطل ينقض بعضه بعضا، والحق يؤيد بعضه بعضاً، والحمد لله على العصمة من الضلالة والتمادي في الغي والجهالة.
And we say: Their doctrine leads to the statement that His power (qudra) is among the attributes of action (sifat al-fi'l). This is because from their doctrine, that which is affirmed and not negated is from the attributes of the self (sifat al-dhat), and that which is affirmed and negated is from the attributes of action. For this reason, they made speech (kalam) from the attributes of action and judged it to be created (muhdath) because it is affirmed and negated: one says He spoke to Moses, peace be upon him, and did not speak to Pharaoh. Similarly here, one says He has power over His own acts and does not have power over the acts of His creatures. So power, according to their statement, becomes from the attributes of action and thus is created, and holding this is unbelief (kufr). If they claim it is created, they abandon their statement that it is from the attributes of the self and that He is powerful by Himself. If they claim it is not created and not from the attributes of action but rather from the attributes of the self (and He was described by it in pre-eternity), then they claim that His power encompasses all possible things (al-maqdurat ajma'), and they have nullified their statement that He does not have power over the acts of His creatures, and they have retracted this issue. If they cling to this issue and affirm their statement that power is from the attributes of the self, then they have nullified for themselves the distinction between attribute of the self and attribute of action according to what they mentioned as a distinction. If they cling to all of that, then they have fallen into the most severe contradiction. Falsehood contradicts itself, while truth supports itself. Praise be to God for protection from misguidance and persistence in error and ignorance.
Source pages p. 891

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed logical argument against the Mu'tazilite position on divine power (qudra). The author first restates his claim: the Mu'tazilite view leads to saying God's power is an attribute of action (sifat al-fi'l) rather than of the self (sifat al-dhat). He then explains their own criterion: an attribute that is both affirmed and negated (e.g., God spoke to Moses but not to Pharaoh) is considered an attribute of action and therefore created (muhdath). They apply this to speech (kalam). Likewise, since they affirm that God has power over His own acts but deny His power over the acts of His creatures (power is both affirmed and negated), power must be an attribute of action and thus created. Calling divine power created is kufr. The author then presents a trilemma: If they say power is created, they abandon their claim that it is from the self. If they say it is not created but from the self, then they must admit God's power encompasses all possible things, nullifying their denial of His power over creatures' acts. If they insist that power is from the self while maintaining their original position, they destroy the very distinction between attribute of self and attribute of action that they themselves set up. Any path leads to contradiction. The author concludes that falsehood is inherently self-contradictory, while truth is consistent.

Key Terms
صفات الذات
صفات الفعل
حادث
قدرة
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is asserting that divine power itself is created.
Correction: The author is not claiming that divine power is created; rather, he is demonstrating that the Mu'tazilite position logically forces that conclusion, which is a clear contradiction of their own principles and is considered kufr.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Mu'tazilite criterion for an attribute being an attribute of action (sifat al-fi'l)?
A) It is affirmed and not negated
B) It is affirmed and negated in different contexts
C) It is always negated
D) It is neither affirmed nor negated

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite criterion for distinguishing attributes of essence from attributes of action, when applied to divine power, forces the conclusion that God's power is created—a position that contradicts their own doctrine and is deemed kufr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held two beliefs that, when carefully examined, contradict each other? What is one area of your faith where you may be defending a position that ultimately undermines God's perfection? Will you today submit to the truth, even if it means admitting you were wrong?
?
The author praises God for protection from misguidance. In what specific way has God protected you from a false belief about His attributes? If you cannot think of one, are you truly grateful for the guidance you have, or do you take it for granted?
?
The Mu'tazilites clung to a distinction that led them to call God's power created. Is there a distinction or compromise in your life that diminishes God's absolute sovereignty—in your thinking, worship, or daily choices? What will you do today to affirm that God is powerful over all—including your own will and actions?

Nasafi's Refutation of the Mu'tazila Attribute Classification
Imam Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila by applying their attribute classification to divine power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila criterion for distinguishing attributes of essence from attributes of act, its application to speech, and why applying it to power leads to an unacceptable conclusion according to Imam Nasafi.

Core Idea
Applying the Mu'tazila's own criterion to divine power forces them into disbelief.

Imam al-Nasafi presents a powerful refutation against the Mu'tazila by turning their own classification of divine attributes against them. He first explains their criterion: attributes that can be both affirmed and negated of God are attributes of act and therefore created. They used this to argue that God's speech is created. Nasafi then applies the same logic to God's power, showing that the Mu'tazila would have to consider power created as well, which contradicts their own doctrine and amounts to disbelief.

Guided Path
1
State the Mu'tazila criterion
Identify the two types of attributes: essence (always affirmed) and act (affirmed and negated).
2
Examine the application to speech
See why they considered speech an attribute of act because it is affirmed for Moses and negated for Pharaoh.
3
Apply the same logic to power
Notice that power is also affirmed for God's own acts but negated for acts of creation, so by their own criterion it would be an attribute of act.
4
Recognize the conclusion
The Mu'tazila believe God's power is eternal and uncreated, but their criterion leads to it being created, which is disbelief.
This shows inconsistency in their position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن من مذهبهم أن ما يثبت ولا ينفى فهو من صفات الذات، وما يثبت وينفى فهو من صفات الفعل، ولهذا جعلوا الكلام من صفات الفعل، وحكموا بكونه محدثًا لما أنه يثبت وينفي فيقال : إنه كلم موسى عليه السلام ولم يكلم فرعون، فكذا هاهنا يقال إنه يقدر على أفعال نفسه ولا يقدر على أفعال خلقه، فتكون القدرة على قضية قولهم من صفات الفعل فيكون حادثًا، والقول بذلك كفر .
Because from their doctrine is that what is affirmed and not negated is of the attributes of essence, and what is affirmed and negated is of the attributes of act. For this reason they made speech from the attributes of act, and ruled that it is temporally originated because it is affirmed and negated: it is said that He spoke to Moses, peace be upon him, and did not speak to Pharaoh. So likewise here it is said that He has power over His own acts and does not have power over the acts of His creation. Thus power, according to the implication of their statement, would be from the attributes of act, and thus would be temporally originated, and saying that is disbelief.
Source pages p. 892

Commentary
This passage presents an argument from Imam al-Nasafi against the Mu'tazila. He first states their principle: what can be both affirmed and negated of God is an attribute of act, while what is only affirmed without negation is an attribute of essence. They applied this to God's speech: God spoke to Moses but not to Pharaoh, so speech can be affirmed and negated, thus it is an attribute of act and therefore created. Imam al-Nasafi then applies the same logic to God's power: it is said that God has power over His own acts but not over the acts of His creation (in the Mu'tazili view), so power too can be affirmed and negated, making it an attribute of act and hence created. But the Mu'tazila hold that God's power is eternal. If they say it is created, that would be disbelief. This is the first step in showing the inconsistency of their position.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is about the meaning of attributes rather than applying the Mu'tazila's own criterion to their own position.
Correction: Imam Nasafi is not redefining attributes; he is using the Mu'tazila's own classification to show an inconsistency in their doctrine.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Mu'tazila criterion for distinguishing attributes of essence from attributes of act?
A) Attributes of essence are those that apply to God alone, attributes of act apply to others.
B) Attributes of essence are those that are affirmed and never negated, attributes of act are those that can be affirmed and negated.
C) Attributes of essence are eternal, attributes of act are created.
D) Attributes of essence are only those mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Imam Nasafi shows that the Mu'tazila criterion for attributes of act, when applied consistently, forces the conclusion that God's power is created, which contradicts their own beliefs and is considered disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila held a standard for divine attributes that, when consistently applied, led to a conclusion they could not accept. In what area of your life might you be applying a double standard—demanding consistency from others while exempting yourself? Will you take the uncomfortable step of examining that inconsistency today?
?
Nasafi's argument shows that even a subtle error in theological method can lead to disbelief. How seriously do you examine the foundations of your own beliefs? Are you willing to follow a line of reasoning to its logical end, even if it challenges comfortable assumptions?
?
This passage is a call to intellectual honesty. Is there a belief you hold simply because it is familiar or widely accepted, rather than because you have rigorously tested it? What would it cost you to either abandon that belief or ground it more firmly? Will you do that today?

Dilemma for Mu'tazila Over Divine Power
Imam Nasafi presents a logical dilemma forcing the Mu'tazila into contradiction over the nature of divine power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi uses a logical dilemma to expose a contradiction in the Mu'tazila's doctrine of divine power.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila's view on divine power collapses into self-contradiction.

Imam Nasafi presents a sharp logical argument against the Mu'tazila. They claim that God's power is an eternal attribute of essence, yet they deny that God has power over human acts. Nasafi shows that these two positions cannot coexist, forcing the Mu'tazila to either abandon their definition of essential attributes or admit that God has power over all things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Nasafi uses a series of conditional statements: 'if they claim... then they abandon...'.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The passage presents two alternatives for the Mu'tazila: either divine power is temporally originated (حادث) or it is not. Trace the consequences of each choice.
3
Understand the contradiction
If power is essential and eternal, it must encompass all possible objects of power, including human acts. But the Mu'tazila deny that God has power over human acts. If power is temporal, then it is not an essential attribute, contradicting their own classification.
This is the core of the dilemma.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that falsehood contradicts itself while truth is consistent. Consider how this principle applies to the Mu'tazila's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن زعموا أنه حادث تركوا قولهم: إنه من صفات الذات وهو قادر بنفسه وإن زعموا أنه ليس بحادث وليس من صفات الفعل بل هو من صفات الذات (وهو كان موصوفا به في الأزل)، فقد زعموا أن قدرته شاملة على المقدورات أجمع وقد أبطلوا قولهم: إنه لا يقدر على أفعال خلقه ورجعوا عن هذه المسألة. وإن تمسكوا بهذه المسألة وتقروا على قولهم: إن القدرة من صفات الذات، فقد أبطلوا على أنفسهم فرقهم بين صفة الذات وصفة الفعل بما ذكروا من الفرق، وإن تمسكوا بكل ذلك فقد ناقضوا أفحش مناقضة، والباطل ينقض بعضه بعضا، والحق يؤيد بعضه بعضاً، والحمد لله على العصمة من الضلالة والتمادي في الغي والجهالة.
If they claim that it is temporally originated, they abandon their statement that it is from the attributes of essence and that He is powerful by Himself. And if they claim that it is not temporally originated and not from the attributes of act, but rather from the attributes of essence (and He was described by it in pre-eternity), then they have claimed that His power encompasses all possible objects of power and have nullified their statement that He does not have power over the acts of His creation, and have retreated from this issue. And if they hold fast to this issue and affirm their statement that power is from the attributes of essence, they have nullified for themselves the distinction they mentioned between the attribute of essence and the attribute of act. And if they hold fast to all of that, they have contradicted themselves most severely. Falsehood contradicts itself, truth supports itself, and praise be to God for protection from misguidance and persistence in error and ignorance.
Source pages p. 892

Commentary
This passage presents a logical dilemma. The Mu'tazila claim that God's power is from the attributes of essence (eternal). But they also claim that God does not have power over the acts of His creation (since they believe in human free will). The dilemma: either they say that power is temporally originated like speech, which contradicts their view that it is an essential attribute; or they say it is not temporally originated and thus is an essential attribute, which would mean His power is all-encompassing (including over human acts), which contradicts their denial that He has power over creation's acts. If they insist on their original claim that power is essential, they nullify their own criterion for distinguishing essential from active attributes (since power can be affirmed and negated). If they try to hold both, they fall into severe contradiction. The conclusion is that falsehood is self-contradictory, while truth is consistent.

Key Terms
حادث
صفات الذات
قادر بنفسه
المقدورات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila's position on divine power is logically consistent.
Correction: Nasafi demonstrates that their position leads to an inescapable contradiction: either power is temporal or eternal, and both options undermine another of their claims.

Checkpoint
What happens if the Mu'tazila concede that power is an essential attribute?
A) They must also say God's power is limited.
B) They must affirm that God has power over the acts of His creation, contradicting their own position.
C) They can still maintain that power is created.
D) They must deny that God is powerful.

Key Takeaway
Falsehood is inherently self-contradictory, while truth is self-consistent; the Mu'tazila's view on divine power exemplifies this principle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah has power over every single action you commit, including your sins? If so, how does that belief change the way you approach repentance—do you rely more on His mercy or your own resolve? What one step will you take today to live in light of His encompassing power?
?
Think of a recent moment when you acted as if your decisions were independent of Allah's will. What contradiction does that reveal in your heart? How can you realign your understanding with the truth that His power encompasses all objects, including your choices?
?
The passage ends with praise for protection from misguidance. In what area of your faith are you at risk of holding contradictory beliefs—perhaps about Allah's attributes or His control over your life? Will you commit this week to studying one attribute more deeply to remove that contradiction?

Refuting the Anthropomorphism Claim: Essential vs. Relational
Imam Nasafi refutes al-Ka'bi's objection by distinguishing essential similarity from accidental relational qualities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi defends the essential similarity between divine and human acts (both bringing from non-existence) against the Mu'tazila charge of tashbih, using the distinction between essential properties and relational names.

Core Idea
Essential similarity is not negated by accidental relational qualities.

This passage presents a critical debate in Sunni-Mu'tazila theology. Al-Ka'bi argues that human acts differ from God's because they are marked by humility or frivolity, while God's acts are wise. Nasafi responds by distinguishing between essential properties and relational names (al-asmā' al-iḍāfiyya), showing that similarity in essence (bringing from non-existence) remains despite accidental differences. You will see how he uses examples like blackness of Zayd and 'Amr to illustrate his point.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the beginning of the passage where the Mu'tazila claim that Nasafi's view implies tashbih between God's act and human acts, both being bringing from non-existence to existence.
This is the core accusation that Nasafi must refute.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
Nasafi cites Quran 16:17 to argue that God denies that anyone has a creation like His. Note how he uses the verse to counter the charge.
The verse is used as a negative proof—God negates any creation like His.
3
Study al-Ka'bi's refinement
Al-Ka'bi objects that human acts have characteristics like humility or frivolity, while God's acts are wise, so there is no resemblance. Understand this intermediate objection.
Al-Ka'bi is a well-known Mu'tazili theologian.
4
Analyze the response on relational names
Nasafi argues that qualities like obedience, disobedience, humility are relational names depending on external factors (e.g., command). They do not affect essential nature.
This is the key philosophical move.
5
Apply the examples
Work through Nasafi's examples: blackness of Zayd and 'Amr are essentially similar despite different owners; stillness and movement differ in essence even with same agent.
These solidify the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قلنا: إنه يؤدي إلى وقوع التشابه بين فعل القديم وفعل الحادث، فإن فعل الله تعالى لما كان إخراجًا من العدم إلى الوجود، وفعل العبد كذلك، كان كل واحد من الفعلين شبيه صاحبه خصوصا على أصلهم فإن عندهم الفعل والمفعول واحد فحركة المرتعش فعل الله ومفعوله وحركة العبد فعل العبد ومفعوله، فلا فرق بين حركة وبين حركة بمعنى من المعاني فكان فعل العبد وخلقه كخلق الله (تعالى وقد قال الله تعالى: أَمْ جَعَلُوا لِلَّهِ شُرَكَاءَ خَلَقُوا كَخَلْقِهِ، فَتَشَبَه الخَلْقُ عَلَيْهِمْ وهذا، والله أعلم استفهام بمعنى الإنكار والنفي، فكان الله تعالى نافيًا أن يكون من أحد خلق كخلقه. فإن قالوا: إن فعلنا وإن كان إخراجًا من العدم إلى الوجود، وفعله تعالى أيضا إخراج من العدم إلى الوجود إلا أنه لا تشابه بين فعلنا وفعله، لأن فعلنا خضوع وذلة أو عبث وفساد وفعله عز وجل حكمة وصواب وليس بخضوع ولا ذلة، والعبث لا يشبه الحكمة. هذا هو اعتراض الكعبي. يقال له : إن الحركة حركة لنفسها، وكذا السكون والسواد والبياض، وكون الفعل طاعة أو معصية أو ذلة أو خضوعاً لمعاني وراء الذات، فإن الفعل يكون طاعة لخروجه على موافقة الأمر، والمعصية تكون معصية لخروج الفعل على مخالفة الأمر وارتكاب ما نهى عنه، فكانا من الأسماء الإضافية، وكذا الحركة لا تكون ذلة لنفسها ، وكذا لا تكون خضوعا لنفسها بل لقصد فاعلها، والقصد معنى في القلب والحركة تكون بالجوارح والمشتبهان لذاتيهما لا يختلفان باعتبار الأسامي الإضافية الثابتة لمعاني هي أغيار للذات. ألا ترى أن سواد زيد وسواد عمرو لا يختلفان لاختلاف المحل، وسكون زيد لا يكون مشابها لحركته وإن كان الفاعل واحدًا لاختلافهما في ذاتيهما، فإذا لم يكن لاتحاد الفاعل أثر في تشابه ما اختلفا بذاتيهما لا يكون لاختلاف الفاعل أو معنى من معانيه أو اختلاف آلة الفاعلين أثر في اختلاف شيئين اشتبها لذاتيهما، وهذا لأن
And we only said that it leads to the occurrence of resemblance between the act of the Eternal and the act of the temporal being. For since the act of God Almighty is a bringing-out from non-existence to existence, and the act of the servant is likewise, each of the two acts is similar to its counterpart, especially according to their own principle, for according to them the act and the object acted are one, so the movement of the tremulous person is God's act and His object acted, and the movement of the servant is the servant's act and his object acted. So there is no difference between a movement and a movement in any sense, so the act of the servant and his creating is like the creation of God Almighty. And God Almighty said: 'Or have they attributed to Allah partners who create like His creation, so the creation became similar to them?' This, and Allah knows best, is an interrogative meaning denial and negation. So God Almighty negated that anyone has a creation like His creation. And if they say: 'Our act, though it is a bringing-out from non-existence to existence, and His act also is a bringing-out from non-existence to existence, yet there is no resemblance between our act and His act, because our act is submissiveness and humility or frivolity and corruption, and His act, Mighty and Majestic, is wisdom and rectitude, not submissiveness nor humility, and frivolity does not resemble wisdom.' This is the objection of al-Ka'bi. It is said to him: Movement is movement in itself, and likewise stillness, blackness, whiteness. And the action being obedience or disobedience or humility or submissiveness is due to meanings beyond the essence. For the action is obedience because it proceeds in compliance with the command, and disobedience is disobedience because the action proceeds in opposition to the command and committing what is forbidden. So they are among relational names. Likewise movement is not humility in itself, nor is it submissiveness in itself, but rather by the intention of its agent, and intention is a meaning in the heart, and movement occurs by the limbs. And two things that are similar in their essences do not differ on account of relational names that are established for meanings other than the essence. Do you not see that the blackness of Zayd and the blackness of 'Amr do not differ due to the difference of location, and the stillness of Zayd is not similar to his movement even if the agent is one, due to their difference in their essences. So if the unity of the agent has no effect in making similar what differ in their essences, then the difference of the agent or a meaning from its meanings or the difference of the instruments of the agents has no effect in differentiating two things that are similar in their essences. And this is because
Source pages p. 892

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila claim that the author's position leads to anthropomorphism (tashbih) by equating God's act (creating from nothing) with human acts. The author first states the objection: since both God and humans bring things from non-existence to existence, their acts are similar. He cites the Quranic verse (13:16) to argue that God denies that anyone has a creation like His. Then he presents al-Ka'bi's objection: human acts are characterized by humility, frivolity, etc., while God's acts are wisdom and rectitude, so there is no similarity. The author responds by analyzing the nature of acts. He argues that movement, blackness, etc. are what they are in themselves. Qualities like obedience, disobedience, humility are relational and depend on external factors (e.g., compliance with command). Two things identical in essence do not differ due to relational names. He gives examples: the blackness of Zayd and 'Amr do not differ because of their owners; stillness and movement of the same person differ in essence. Therefore, if two acts are similar in their essences (both bringing from non-existence to existence), they remain similar regardless of the differences in agent or accidental qualities. Thus the Mu'tazila objection fails because it confuses essential similarity with accidental differences.

Key Terms
التشابه
فعل القديم
فعل الحادث
إخراج من العدم
الأسماء الإضافية
القصد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Essential similarity between divine and human acts implies complete identity in all respects.
Correction: Nasafi shows that similarity in the essential property of bringing from non-existence does not mean all accidental qualities are shared; relational names like obedience/humility are independent of essence.

Checkpoint
According to the response to al-Ka'bi, why does the obedience or disobedience of an action not affect its essential nature?
A) Because obedience and disobedience are essential to the action itself.
B) Because obedience and disobedience are relational names dependent on external factors like command.
C) Because God's actions are always wise.
D) Because human actions are always flawed.

Key Takeaway
Essential similarity of acts (both being bringing from non-existence) is not negated by accidental relational qualities like obedience or humility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone commit a sin you have also committed, do you immediately think your sin is somehow different because of your intention? How does this lesson's distinction between essence and relational qualities challenge you to be honest about the similarity of your own faults?
?
Is there a relationship in your life where you have judged another person's action as 'bad' based only on its external form, ignoring that the same act done by you might seem 'good' because of your intention? How will you change that starting today?
?
If two actions are essentially the same (e.g., both are speech), but one is backbiting and the other is sincere advice, what does this lesson demand of you in terms of examining your own heart before speaking? Will you commit to assessing your intentions before acting?
