Nasafi's Refutation and the True Nature of Divine and Human Power
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite view and presents the correct doctrine of power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that the Mu'tazilite view leads to the nullification of divine power and his alternative explanation of how power attaches to actions.

Core Idea
If power only attaches to existence, and existence is not additional to essence, then power attaches to nothing—nullifying all divine power.

In this lesson, Nasafi builds on the Mu'tazilite premise to show its absurd consequences. He argues that if power attaches only to existence and existence is not an additional attribute, then power can attach to nothing, which would nullify the Creator and imply the preeternity of the world. Then he presents the Ash'ari-Maturidi position: God creates the thingness and existence of all things, while the servant's power attaches to the specific qualities like movement and obedience.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic refutation
Read the Arabic passage from 'ثم قدرة الفاعل لا تتعلق إلا بالوجود' to the end. Identify Nasafi's logical steps.
2
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
Nasafi shows that if existence is not additional to essence, and power only attaches to existence, then power attaches to nothing. This leads to five consequences: nullification of Maker, preeternity of world, etc.
These consequences are listed.
3
Understand Nasafi's alternative
Read his positive statement: God creates existence and thingness; human power attaches to the specific characterization (being movement, obedience, etc.).
This resolves the problem.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد بينا أنه معقول لقيام الدلائل العقلية عليه إلا أنه ليس بموهوم، ولو رفضت المعتزلة التعصب ونظرت بالعقل وانقادت للدليل وجانبت الهوى وأنصفت من نفسها لعرفت أنهم القائلون بما لا يعقل المستمسكون بما هو المحال الممتنع، وذلك أن من مذهب جمهورهم أن المعدوم شيء، وأكثرهم يزعمون أنه عين وعرض وجوهر قبل الحدوث وكذا سواد وحركة وذات على ما قررنا قبل هذا من بيان أقاويلهم. ثم قدرة الفاعل لا تتعلق إلا بالوجود ولا تعلق لها بالشيئية، ولا تكون حركة ولا سوادا ولا جوهرًا ولا ذاتاً ولا عينا لأن هذه الأوصاف كانت ثابتة في الأزل، ثم الوجود ليس بمعنى وراء الذات ولا تعلق للقدرة بالذات فلا يتصور تعلقها بالوجود إذ هو ليس معنى وراء الذات فإذا لا تعلق القدرة ما، لا للقدرة القديمة ولا للقدرة المحدثة بمقدور البتة، وفيه تعطيل الصانع والقول بقدم العالم، وإبطال ثبوت الفعل للعباد، وتعطيل الأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، ونحن نقول: إن الله تعالى خلق العالم وجعل ما ليس بسواد ولا بياض ولا جوهر ولا عرض ولا موجود سوادًا وبياضا وجوهرًا وعرضاً وموجودًا، ثم ما كان من ذلك أفعال العباد فوجوده وشيئيته متعلقة بقدرة الله تعالى وكونه حركة وسكونا وطاعة ومعصية متعلقة بقدرة العبد، وعندهم لا تتعلق شيئية بقدرة أحد ووجوده ليس بمعنى وراء الشيئية، فينبغي أن لا تتعلق قدرة العبد به فلم يمكنهم تعليق قدرة العبد إلا بقدر ما قلنا.
We have explained that it is rational because rational proofs are established upon it, except that it is not imaginary. And if the Mu'tazila abandoned partisanship, looked with reason, submitted to the proof, shunned desire, and were fair to themselves, they would know that they are the ones saying what is not rational, holding onto what is impossible and absurd. That is because the doctrine of most of them is that the non-existent is a thing, and most of them claim that it is an entity (ayn), an accident, a substance before coming into existence, similarly blackness, movement, and essence (dhat) according to what we have previously recorded in explaining their sayings. Then the power of the agent does not attach except to existence, and has no attachment to thingness (shay'iyya), and it does not become movement, blackness, substance, essence, or entity because these attributes were established in preeternity. Then existence is not a meaning additional to the essence, and power has no attachment to the essence, so its attachment to existence is inconceivable since it is not a meaning additional to the essence. Thus power attaches to nothing, neither the eternal power nor the temporally originated power attaches to any object of power (maqdur) at all. In this is the nullification of the Maker, the statement of the preeternity of the world, the annulment of the establishment of action for servants, and the nullification of command, prohibition, promise, and threat. And we say: God Almighty created the world and made what is not blackness, whiteness, substance, accident, or existence into blackness, whiteness, substance, accident and existence. Then whatever of that is the actions of servants, their existence and thingness are attached to the power of God Almighty, and their being movement, stillness, obedience, and disobedience are attached to the power of the servant. According to them, thingness is not attached to anyone's power, and existence is not a meaning additional to thingness, so it is necessary that the power of the servant does not attach to it, so they could not attach the power of the servant except to what we said.
Source pages p. 919

Commentary
This passage presents a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that the non-existent (ma'dum) is a thing (shay') and that power (qudra) attaches only to existence. The author begins by stating that the issue is rationally clear, but the Mu'tazila are blinded by partisanship. He describes their doctrine: they claim the non-existent is a thing, and even assign to it attributes like being an entity, substance, or accident before existence. Then he argues that if power attaches only to existence, and existence is not additional to the essence, then power cannot attach to the essence either, leading to the conclusion that power attaches to nothing. This would nullify divine power entirely, implying preeternity of the world and negation of actions for servants. To counter this, the author states his own position: God creates the world and brings non-existent attributes into existence; for human actions, the existence and thingness depend on God's power while the specific quality (movement, stillness, obedience) depends on human power. The Mu'tazila, by denying thingness as an object of power, cannot consistently attribute any power to the servant except as the author has stated.

Key Terms
القدرة
الوجود
الذات
المقدور
الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite view that power attaches only to existence is harmless.
Correction: Nasafi shows it leads to denying all divine and human power, undermining the entire religious framework.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the consequence of the Mu'tazilite view that power attaches only to existence?
A) It affirms the world's creation in time.
B) It nullifies the Maker and implies the world's preeternity.
C) It proves human free will.
D) It establishes the reality of accidents.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi disproves the Mu'tazilite theory by showing it leads to the denial of all power, and he replaces it with a two-tiered account of divine and human causal roles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that Allah creates the very existence of your actions, and only their moral quality is from you, does this humble you or make you more conscious of your accountability? How will you change your intention before each action starting today?
?
The passage shows that denying even one attribute of Allah can lead to nullifying all His power. Have you ever trivialized any of Allah's attributes in your mind? What will you do to guard your understanding of His names and attributes from this lesson?
?
If your power is limited only to the specific characterization of your actions (movement, stillness, etc.), are you tempted to feel that your choices are insignificant? Conversely, how does knowing that Allah gives existence to your choices encourage you to strive for obedience?

The Principle of Action: Creation and Acquisition
Nasafi presents the principle of action attribution using the example of movement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi principle that a single action can be attributed to both Allah as Creator and to the human as Acquirer.

Core Idea
Actions are created by Allah and acquired by humans.

Before addressing the specific question of kufr, Nasafi establishes a foundational principle: when a movement involves both a Creator and a human agent, it is considered an act of both—Allah creates it and the human acquires it. This principle is essential for understanding how sinful actions can be attributed to humans without attributing evil to Allah. Read the passage to see how he illustrates this with the example of wind and movers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with attention to the example
The passage uses the example of wind and two movers. Notice how the same movement is described as both an act of Allah (praised) and an act of the human (blamed).
The principle is that attribution depends on the agent's role: creation vs. acquisition.
2
Identify the key distinction
Nasafi distinguishes between the act as creation (فعل الله) and as acquisition (فعل العبد). This distinction is central to Maturidi theology.
3
Apply the principle to the broader debate
Think about how this principle will be used to answer the objection about kufr. The principle allows that an evil act can be created by Allah (good in creation) but acquired by the human (evil in intention).
This prepares for the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحد منهما عليها ويثاب ويذم العاصي منهما عليها ويعاقب، وكذا لو كان المحركين الريح كانت الحركة في نفسها فعلاً الله تعالى ويحمد عليه وفعلاً للمحرك المنهى عنه ومعصية منه يذم عليها ويعاقب، وإن لم تكن هي متجزئة في نفسها، والله الموفق. وبهذا يجابون عن قولهم: إن الكافر من فعله الكفر. قلنا: نحن نسلم هذا، ولكن عندنا الكفر فعل الكافر لا فعل الله تعالى وإنما هو مفعوله، ومن سلم لكم أن الكفر فعل الله تعالى من النجارية ومتكلمي أهل الحديث فإنهم يمنعون أن يكون الكافر من كان الكفر فعله ويقولون: الكافر من كان الكفر فعله، ويقولون: من قام به الكفر لا من فعل الكفر كما أن المتحرك من قامت به الحركة لا من فعل الحركة والميت من قام به الموت لا من فعل الموت، وكذا هذا في السواد والبياض والحرارة والبرودة والحلاوة والحموضة والطول والقصر، فإما ما تزعمون أن الميت المريض الطويل القصير الأسود الأبيض الحار البارد الحلو الحامض هو الله تعالى لكون هذه المعاني فعلاً له فتنسلخون عن الدين، وإما أن تقروا بتناقض مذهبكم وبطلان شبهتكم.
One of them is praised and the disobedient one of them is blamed and punished, and likewise if the movers of the wind: the movement in itself is an act of Allah, praised for it, and an act of the mover forbidden and a disobedience from him for which he is blamed and punished, even if it is not divisible in itself. And Allah is the grantor of success. And with this they answer their statement: 'The disbeliever is the one whose act is kufr.' We say: we accept this, but in our view kufr is the act of the disbeliever, not the act of Allah, rather it is His created thing. And whoever concedes to you that kufr is the act of Allah among the Najjariyya and the speculative theologians of the People of Hadith, they prevent that the disbeliever is the one whose act is kufr, and they say: the disbeliever is the one from whom kufr proceeds, and they say: the one in whom kufr inheres, not the one who does kufr, just as the moving thing is the one in which movement inheres, not the one who does movement, and the dead is the one in whom death inheres, not the one who does death. And likewise this applies to blackness, whiteness, heat, cold, sweetness, sourness, tallness, shortness. So either you claim that the dead, the sick, the tall, the short, the black, the white, the hot, the cold, the sweet, the sour is Allah because these meanings are His act, and then you divest yourselves of religion, or you admit the contradiction of your doctrine and the falsity of your argument.
Source pages p. 923

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. It begins by stating a principle: when two agents are involved in a movement (e.g., Allah as creator and the human as actor), the movement is considered an act of Allah in terms of creation (praised), and an act of the human in terms of acquisition (blamed if forbidden). Using this principle, the author answers the objection that the disbeliever is the one who does kufr. The Maturidis accept that kufr is the act of the disbeliever, but they clarify: kufr is the act of the disbeliever as acquisition (kasb), not as creation. The Najjariyya and some hadith scholars go further, arguing that names like 'disbeliever' refer to the one in whom kufr inheres, not the one who creates it, analogous to 'moving' referring to the thing that moves, not the creator of movement. This leads to a dilemma: if attributes like tallness and sweetness are acts of Allah, then applying them to creatures would force the opponent to say Allah has those attributes, which is absurd. Thus the opponent's position is contradictory.

Key Terms
فعل
مفعول
كسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidis believe humans do not truly act; Allah does everything.
Correction: This passage shows that humans truly acquire actions, and are held responsible for them.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the movement as an act of Allah and as an act of the human?
A) They are two different movements
B) They are the same movement considered from different perspectives
C) The human creates the movement
D) Allah does not create sinful actions

Key Takeaway
A single action can be attributed to Allah as Creator and to the human as Acquirer, explaining human responsibility without attributing evil to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever committed a sin and then blamed your circumstances or even Allah for it, forgetting that while Allah created the action, you acquired it? How does this principle change your accountability before Allah?
?
In what areas of your life do you need to take more ownership of your actions, knowing that you are the acquirer and will be held responsible?
?
How does knowing that disobedience is your own acquisition affect your repentance? Does it make you more humble or more desperate for Allah's mercy?

Answering the Objection: Kufr as the Act of the Disbeliever
Nasafi responds to the objection about kufr and introduces the Najjariyya view, culminating in a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidis respond to the objection that kufr is the act of the disbeliever, and the dilemma posed to the Najjariyya position.

Core Idea
Kufr is the disbeliever's act by acquisition, not creation.

Having established the principle of action attribution, Nasafi now applies it to the specific objection: 'The disbeliever is the one whose act is kufr.' He accepts this but clarifies the nature of the attribution. Then he presents a stronger view from the Najjariyya and Hadith scholars, leading to a powerful dilemma that exposes the contradiction in the opponents' argument. Read carefully to follow the logical steps.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the key claims
Nasafi accepts the objection's wording but redefines it. Note how he distinguishes between 'act' (فعل) and 'created thing' (مفعول).
2
Understand the Najjariyya position
The Najjariyya go further: they say 'disbeliever' refers to the one in whom kufr inheres, not the one who creates it. They use analogies like movement and death.
This is a different theological school.
3
Analyse the dilemma
Nasafi presents a dilemma: either you say Allah is dead, sick, etc. (absurd), or you admit your argument is contradictory. Understand why this follows.
This refutation depends on the analogy.

?

Creation of Evil is Not Evil
Nasafi begins to argue that creation of evil is not evil, citing lack of human origination power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that the creation of evil is not itself evil, based on the premise that only Allah has the power of origination.

Core Idea
Creating evil is not evil because only Allah originates all things.

Nasafi addresses a profound theological question: If Allah creates all things, including evil acts, does that make Him evil? In this passage, he begins to argue that the creation of evil is not morally evil, because evil is a quality of the act itself, not of its creation. The key premise is that human beings lack the power to originate (ikhtira')—only Allah can bring something into existence from nothing. This foundational idea shapes the rest of his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Pay attention to the key terms: إيجاد القبيح, السفه, الاختراع.
The passage is cut off mid-sentence, but the core argument is clear.
2
Identify the two proofs referenced
The passage refers to 'the two proofs' that the servant has an act but no power of origination. Understand the distinction between action (fi'l) and origination (ikhtira').
This distinction is crucial for the argument.
3
Trace the logical conclusion
From the premise that only Allah originates, Nasafi concludes that every event is His creation. Therefore, the creation of evil is not evil, because evil is a quality of the act itself, not of its creation.
The argument is incomplete, but the logical chain is clear from the given text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إيجاد القبيح ليس بقبيح: وكذا من تمسك بالدليلين أعنى ما مر أن العبد له فعل وليست له قدرة الاختراع وعرف فساد قولهم إن إيجاد القبيح قبيح وإيجاد السفه سفه لأن الدليل الذي دل أن لا اختراع إلا من الله تعالى يوجب أن كل حادث كان باختراعه، وقيام
The creation of evil is not evil: And likewise, whoever adheres to the two proofs, namely what has passed that the servant has an act and does not have the power of origination (ikhtira'), and knows the corruption of their statement that the creation of evil is evil and the creation of foolishness is foolishness, because the proof that there is no origination except from Allah necessitates that every incident is by His origination, and the establishment...
Source pages p. 924

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of an argument that creating evil is not itself evil. It references two proofs previously mentioned: that the servant has an act but not the power to originate (ikhtira'). Since only Allah can originate, and He creates everything, the act of creating evil is not evil; rather, evil is a description of the act itself, not of the creation of it. The text is incomplete, cutting off at 'and the establishment' (wa qiyam).

Key Terms

السفه
الاختراع
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If Allah creates evil deeds, then He is evil.
Correction: Nasafi argues that creation of evil is not evil because evil is a moral quality of the act itself, not of its creation. Since only Allah originates, and He creates all acts, the act of creation is neutral; the moral quality belongs to the act's nature.

Checkpoint
What premise does Nasafi use to argue that creating evil is not evil?
A) The servant has no power to originate
B) Evil is defined by human intention
C) Allah does not create evil at all
D) Evil is only in the afterlife

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's argument hinges on the distinction between the act of creation and the moral quality of the created act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you feel that you are the ultimate originator of that act, or do you recognize that Allah creates the act and you merely acquire it? How does this truth change your sense of pride or shame? Will you humbly repent and attribute both your good and bad actions to Allah's creation?
?
If you truly believe that Allah's creation of evil is not evil, then why do you still find yourself complaining about the evil in your life? Are you willing to stop accusing Allah of wrongdoing when you face hardship? This week, when a trial comes, will you say, 'This is from Allah, and it is not evil in itself'?
?
You often judge others' actions as evil. But do you ever think that Allah created that person's action, and yet the person is responsible because they performed it? How does this lesson make you more humble in judging others? Will you commit to withholding final judgment, since only Allah knows the full reality of creation?

Proof that God is Wise and Refutation of Mu'tazilites
Nasafi proves God's wisdom in all actions and refutes Mu'tazilite classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that God is wise in all actions and how this refutes the Mu'tazilite misunderstanding of wisdom and foolishness.

Core Idea
God's wisdom encompasses all creation; human judgments of foolishness are limited.

Imam Nasafi presents a concise yet powerful argument for God's absolute wisdom. He begins by stating that the proof of God's wisdom entails that every created thing, whether judged good or evil by humans, is wise in purpose. This immediately challenges the Mu'tazilite assumption that some actions are foolish. In this lesson, we will unpack his reasoning and see why the Mu'tazilite position collapses under its own limited perspective.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the assertive tone: the proof 'requires' something.
2
Identify the core claim
Nasafi states that God is wise in all He creates, regardless of human evaluation. What does this imply about Mu'tazilite categories?
3
Understand the refutation
The Mu'tazilites are said to be ignorant of true wisdom and foolishness because their intellects are deficient. Why is this a powerful critique?
4
Grasp the concluding point
The claim to know all divine wisdoms is falsified by intuition (البداهة). What does 'intuition' mean here?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدليل على كونه عز وجل حكيمًا يوجب أنه تعالى في جميع ما أوجده حكيم، قبيحاً كان ذلك الموجد أو حسنًا سفها كان أو حكمة، وعرف بذلك أن ما يظنه المعتزلة حكمًا وسفها ليس كما ظنوا ، وأنهم جاهلون بحقيقة الحكمة والسفه إذ الجهل عليهم جائز ممكن والخطأ على ما أقمنا من الدليل ممتنع ، والحاصل أنهم يحكمون بكون ما لا اطلاع لهم على وجه الحكمة بالسفه، وهذا جهل إذ عقولهم قاصرة عن كثير من الحكم البشرية، ودعوى الاطلاع على جميع الحكم الربوبية دعوى ظهر فسادها للبداهة، والله الموفق.
The proof that He, Might and Majestic, is wise requires that He, Exalted, is wise in all that He creates, whether that created thing is evil or good, foolishness or wisdom. And it is known by that that what the Mu'tazilites suppose to be wisdom and foolishness is not as they supposed, and that they are ignorant of the reality of wisdom and foolishness, since ignorance is possible and permissible for them, and error is impossible according to what we have established of proof. The upshot is that they judge that what they have no knowledge of its aspect of wisdom is foolishness, and this is ignorance, since their intellects are deficient with respect to many human wisdoms, and the claim of having knowledge of all divine wisdoms is a claim whose falsity is evident by intuition. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 925

Commentary
This passage is a proof of God's wisdom and a refutation of the Mu'tazilite misunderstanding. It begins by asserting that the proof that God is wise entails that He is wise in all created things, whether they appear good or evil, wise or foolish. Then it explains that this clarifies that the Mu'tazilite classification of things as wise or foolish is mistaken. They are ignorant of the true nature of wisdom and foolishness, and their judgment is flawed because it is possible for them to be ignorant and error is impossible from God. The passage concludes that the Mu'tazilites' claim to know all divine wisdoms is obviously false; human intellects are limited even with respect to human wisdoms.

Key Terms
حكيم
حكمة
سفه
قبيح
البداهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some actions of God appear pointless or evil, implying God may be foolish.
Correction: Nasafi argues that apparent foolishness is due to human ignorance; all divine actions are wise by definition, and it is impossible for God to act foolishly.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, how does the Mu'tazilite claim to know all divine wisdoms stand?
A) It is evident by intuition.
B) Its falsity is evident by intuition.
C) It is supported by revealed texts.
D) It is a necessary truth.

Key Takeaway
God's wisdom covers all creation; human judgments of foolishness are a result of intellectual limitation, not divine imperfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness events in your life that seem unfair or pointless, do you secretly think God could have done better? What does this passage demand you to change?
?
The Mu'tazilites assumed they could judge God's actions. Where in your daily life do you similarly assume you know better than God's plan? What would it cost you to surrender that assumption?
?
Nasafi says even human wisdoms are beyond full grasp, let alone divine. How does this humility apply to your own judgments of others' actions? Will you now pause before labeling someone's act as foolish?

The Maturidi Definition of Wisdom and Foolishness
Nasafi states the Maturidi definition of hikma and safah by outcome.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi definitions of wisdom (ḥikma) and foolishness (safah) as determined by the outcome of actions.

Core Idea
Wisdom is measured by the outcome, not by the doer's benefit.

The Maturidi scholars defined wisdom and foolishness in a way that centers on the outcome (ʿāqiba). This definition is crucial for understanding how God's actions are all wise, even if we do not see immediate benefit. In this lesson, we examine their precise formulation.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of wisdom
Read the Arabic passage where Nasafi states that everything with a praiseworthy outcome is wisdom. Notice that wisdom is linked to 'āqiba ḥamīda.
The definition is straightforward: good outcome = wisdom.
2
Identify the two types of foolishness
The passage gives two reasons why an act can be foolish: either it lacks a praiseworthy outcome, or it has a harmful outcome without any compensating good.
Foolishness is not limited to harmful acts; even acts with no benefit are foolish.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the Maturidis define wisdom and foolishness by outcome rather than by the agent's intention or need. This sets the stage for discussions about divine actions.
This definition allows that God's actions are always wise even if their benefit is not apparent to us.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما مشايخنا رحمهم الله فإنهم قالوا كل ما له عاقبة حميدة فهو وجه حكمة، وما ليست له عاقبة حميدة فهو سفه وقبيح، وما تعلقت به عاقبة وخيمة فهو سفه لوجهين أحدهما خلو نفس الفعل عن العاقبة الحميدة، والآخر : خلو تحمل ذلك المعنى الوخيم عن العاقبة والحكمة ما تعلقت به عاقبة حميدة، والكلام في بيان صحة هذا الحديث مذكور في تصنيف لي في هذه المسألة على حدة لا إلى ذكره هاهنا لما فيه من الطول وبنا غنية عن ذلك إنما حاجتنا إلى إبطال شبه الخصوم وتسويتهم بين الشاهد والغائب، وقد بينا ذلك وقد سبق القول في إبطال مذاهب الثنوية، أن الله خلق ما لا يحصى كثرة مما لا انتفاع لأحد من خلقه به ولا اطلاع لممتحن عليه من الأجزاء الكامنة في تخوم الأرضين وبواطن الجبال وقعور البحار وهو تعالى يجل عن الانتفاع بشيء، ومع ذلك لم يكن خلق ذلك عبثا، على أن الاستدلال بالشاهد محال أيضا لما أن كل فاعل في الشاهد محل الحاجات والضرورات، فإذا اشتغل بما لا نفع له به وهو محتاج إلى اجتلاب المنافع ودفع المضار فكان اشتغاله به إعراضا عما فيه جلبة منفعة له ودفع مضرة، فكان ذلك منه رضا بالنقيصة وتحمل المضرة فكان سفها، والله تعالى يجل عن ذلك فلم يكن
As for our teachers—may God have mercy on them—they said: everything that has a praiseworthy outcome is an aspect of wisdom, and everything that does not have a praiseworthy outcome is foolishness and ugly. And that to which a harmful outcome is attached is foolishness for two reasons: one is the emptiness of the action itself from a praiseworthy outcome, and the other is the emptiness of bearing that harmful meaning from a good outcome. And wisdom is that to which a praiseworthy outcome is attached. The discussion of demonstrating the correctness of this statement is mentioned in my separate treatise on this issue, and we do not need to mention it here due to its length; our need is only to refute the doubts of the opponents and their equating between the witnessed and the unseen, and we have already explained that. And the discourse on refuting the doctrines of the Thunawiyya has preceded: that God created an innumerable multitude of things from which no one of His creation benefits, and no examinant has knowledge of them—such as particles hidden in the depths of the earth, the interiors of mountains, and the bottoms of seas—and He is exalted above benefiting from anything. Nevertheless, that creation was not futile. Moreover, reasoning from the witnessed is impossible because every agent in the witnessed is subject to needs and necessities; if he occupies himself with what is of no benefit to him while he needs to attract benefits and repel harms, then his occupation with it is a turning away from what brings him benefit and repels harm, so that is from him a contentment with deficiency and a bearing of harm, and thus it is foolishness. And God Almighty is exalted above that, and it is not...
Source pages p. 928

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi (mashāyikh) definition of wisdom (ḥikma) and foolishness (safah). According to them, ḥikma is that which has a good outcome (‘āqiba ḥamīda), while safah is that which lacks a good outcome or has a harmful outcome. Foolishness is twofold: either the act itself has no good outcome, or it has a harmful outcome without compensating benefit. The author notes that a full proof is in another work; here his goal is only to refute the analogy between shahid and ghā’ib. He then gives an example: God created countless things that benefit no one and are unknown, yet this is not futile. He contrasts this with human agents, who act out of need; engaging in useless acts would be foolish. God is exalted above such need, so His actions cannot be judged by human standards.

Key Terms
مشايخ
حكمة
سفه
عاقبة حميدة
عاقبة وخيمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that foolishness only applies when an act harms the doer.
Correction: The Maturidi definition includes acts with no beneficial outcome at all as foolish, not only those that cause harm.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi definition, an act with a harmful outcome is foolish because:
A) It has a harmful outcome, which is always bad.
B) It lacks a praiseworthy outcome and bearing the harm has no compensation.
C) It is always ugly regardless of outcome.
D) It benefits no one.

Key Takeaway
Wisdom and foolishness are defined by the outcome: praiseworthy outcome makes an act wise; its absence or a harmful outcome makes it foolish.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own decisions, do you measure them by their outcomes? Which decision in your life right now needs to be re-evaluated not by its immediate result but by whether it will lead to a praiseworthy outcome in the sight of Allah?
?
You believe that Allah is al-Hakīm (the All-Wise). But when you face trials that seem to have no good outcome, do you truly trust that His wisdom is at work? What would change in your heart if you fully embraced that every act of Allah has a praiseworthy outcome, even if hidden?
?
This lesson defines foolishness as any action that lacks a praiseworthy outcome. Reflect on your daily habits: which actions are you doing that, honestly, have no good outcome for your Hereafter? Will you commit to dropping at least one such action today?

Refuting the Analogy Between Human and Divine Acts
Nasafi refutes the analogy between witnessed and unseen and gives the example of God's creation of hidden particles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's creation of seemingly useless things is not foolish, and why the analogy between human and divine actions is invalid.

Core Idea
God's actions cannot be judged by human standards because He is free of need.

Having defined wisdom and foolishness, Nasafi now addresses a key objection: if wisdom requires a praiseworthy outcome, how can God create countless things that seem to have no benefit? He argues that the analogy between human agents and God is flawed because humans act out of need while God is utterly self-sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Understand the refutation approach
Nasafi first acknowledges that a full proof of the definition exists elsewhere, but his aim here is to refute the opponents' doubt that equates the witnessed (shāhid) with the unseen (ghā'ib).
He builds on a previous refutation of dualist doctrines.
2
Examine the example of hidden creation
Read the part about God creating countless particles in the earth, mountains, and seas that no one benefits from or knows about. Nasafi states this creation was not futile (ʿabath).
This example shows that God's actions can be wise even without apparent benefit to creation.
3
Learn why human analogy fails
Nasafi explains that human agents are needy: they must seek benefit and avoid harm. If they engage in useless acts, it is foolish. But God is exalted above such needs, so the analogy is invalid.
The key difference is need (ḥājāt) vs. self-sufficiency (ghinā).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما مشايخنا رحمهم الله فإنهم قالوا كل ما له عاقبة حميدة فهو وجه حكمة، وما ليست له عاقبة حميدة فهو سفه وقبيح، وما تعلقت به عاقبة وخيمة فهو سفه لوجهين أحدهما خلو نفس الفعل عن العاقبة الحميدة، والآخر : خلو تحمل ذلك المعنى الوخيم عن العاقبة والحكمة ما تعلقت به عاقبة حميدة، والكلام في بيان صحة هذا الحديث مذكور في تصنيف لي في هذه المسألة على حدة لا إلى ذكره هاهنا لما فيه من الطول وبنا غنية عن ذلك إنما حاجتنا إلى إبطال شبه الخصوم وتسويتهم بين الشاهد والغائب، وقد بينا ذلك وقد سبق القول في إبطال مذاهب الثنوية، أن الله خلق ما لا يحصى كثرة مما لا انتفاع لأحد من خلقه به ولا اطلاع لممتحن عليه من الأجزاء الكامنة في تخوم الأرضين وبواطن الجبال وقعور البحار وهو تعالى يجل عن الانتفاع بشيء، ومع ذلك لم يكن خلق ذلك عبثا، على أن الاستدلال بالشاهد محال أيضا لما أن كل فاعل في الشاهد محل الحاجات والضرورات، فإذا اشتغل بما لا نفع له به وهو محتاج إلى اجتلاب المنافع ودفع المضار فكان اشتغاله به إعراضا عما فيه جلبة منفعة له ودفع مضرة، فكان ذلك منه رضا بالنقيصة وتحمل المضرة فكان سفها، والله تعالى يجل عن ذلك فلم يكن

And that to which a harmful outcome is attached is foolishness for two reasons: one is the emptiness of the action itself from a praiseworthy outcome, and the other is the emptiness of bearing that harmful meaning from a good outcome. And wisdom is that to which a praiseworthy outcome is attached. The discussion of demonstrating the correctness of this statement is mentioned in my separate treatise on this issue, and we do not need to mention it here due to its length; our need is only to refute the doubts of the opponents and their equating between the witnessed and the unseen, and we have already explained that. And God Almighty is exalted above that, and it is not...

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi (mashāyikh) definition of wisdom (ḥikma) and foolishness (safah). He contrasts this with human agents, who act out of need; engaging in useless acts would be foolish. God is exalted above such need, so His actions cannot be judged by human standards.

Key Takeaway
God's actions cannot be judged by human standards because God is free of need; thus, even creation without apparent benefit is not foolish.

?

?
Nasafi says that a needy human who does something useless is content with deficiency and foolish. In what area of your life are you acting as if your own benefit is the ultimate measure of worth—perhaps in your worship, relationships, or daily choices? Confess that tendency to God and ask Him to purify your intentions.
?
If you truly believed that God’s actions are never futile, even when they bring no visible benefit to you, how would your response to unanswered prayers or unexplained suffering change? Write down one specific situation where you need to adopt this mindset starting today.

The Arrogance of Requiring Comprehension of God's Wisdom
The author refutes the objection that God's wisdom must be comprehensible to humans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is arrogant to insist that God's wisdom must be comprehensible to human reason.

Core Idea
Limiting God's wisdom to human understanding is arrogance.

This passage presents a powerful refutation of those who claim they would understand God's wisdom if it existed. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, points out that human minds are incapable even of grasping all human wisdoms, so how can they set themselves as judges over divine commands? This lesson will unpack the logic of this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the flow of objection and refutation.
Notice the structure: 'For if they claim... then they have been arrogant...'
2
Identify the objection and the refutation
The objectors claim that if there were wisdom in God's actions, they would know it. The author refutes by calling this arrogance and providing a reason: human minds are limited.
The refutation is not just a denial but a reasoned argument.
3
Analyze the key terms
Focus on 'istikbar' (arrogance) and 'qanun' (standard/measure). The author accuses them of making their own limited minds the standard for divine judgments.
This highlights the principle of tanzih (transcendence).
4
Reflect on the implication
Understand the theological principle: human reason is not the measure of divine wisdom. This guards against anthropomorphism and rationalist overreach in theology.
This is a foundational concept in Maturidi kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن زعموا أنه لو كانت فيه حكمة لعقلوها ووقفوا عليها؛ فقد استكبروا في أنفسهم وعتوا عتوا كبيرًا حيث جعلوا عقولهم القاصرة عن الوقوف على بعض الحكم البشرية قانونا للحكم الربوبية.
For if they claim that if there were wisdom in it, they would have comprehended it and known it; then they have been arrogant in themselves and have become greatly insolent, for they have made their minds, which are incapable of understanding some human wisdoms, a standard for divine judgments.
Source pages p. 929

Commentary
This passage is an objection and its refutation. The objectors (likely Mu'tazila or others) claim that if there were wisdom in God's actions (e.g., creating evil), they would have comprehended it. The author refutes by calling this arrogance (istikbār) and insolence (ʿutuww). The reasoning is that human minds are even incapable of understanding some human wisdoms, so how can they set their limited reason as a standard (qānūn) for divine judgments (al-ḥukm al-rubūbiyya)? This guards against anthropocentrism in theology.

Key Terms
حكمة
استكبروا
عتوا
قانون
الحكم الربوبية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's wisdom must be fully comprehensible to human reason.
Correction: Human reason is limited and cannot fully grasp divine wisdom; to demand comprehension is arrogance.

Checkpoint
What does the author accuse those who claim they would comprehend God's wisdom of?
A) Ignorance.
B) Arrogance and insolence.
C) Proper inquiry.
D) Following the Dualists.

Key Takeaway
Human reason is insufficient to judge divine wisdom; to demand comprehension is arrogance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Where in your life have you set your own understanding as the judge of what God should do? Will you today repent from that arrogance and accept that His wisdom is beyond your limited mind?
?
You claim to trust God, but do you truly trust that His wisdom is good even when it makes no sense to you? What concrete step can you take this week to act on that trust without needing to comprehend it first?

The First Wisdom: Perfect Power through Opposites
Enumeration of the first wisdom for creating evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God's creation of both good and evil actions demonstrates His perfect power and distinguishes His eternal power from temporal power.

Core Idea
Creating opposites proves perfect power, because only God can do so.

The author begins by stating that the wisdoms behind God's creation of disbelief and sin are countless. He then focuses on the first wisdom: by creating both good and evil actions, God displays His perfect power and effective will. This lesson explores how creating opposites (like good/evil, pure/impure) is a sign of unlimited power, and how this relates to the distinction between God's eternal power and the temporal power of creatures.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the structure: it begins with a general statement, then presents the first wisdom with its supporting argument, analogy, and additional point.
2
Understand the first wisdom
Identify the wisdom: God creates good and evil actions to show His perfect power and effective will, as He can create opposites.
The proof is that if an agent can only produce one type of thing, it is constrained.
3
Examine the analogy
Notice the analogy with the creation of bodies with opposite qualities (good/evil, pure/impure, etc.) which is said to be profound wisdom.
4
Grasp the additional point
Understand that this also manifests God's power over the acts of others, distinguishing eternal power from temporal power and comprehensive will from limited will.
This establishes God's absolute sovereignty and independence.
5
Reflect on God's independence
The passage concludes by stating that God is powerful over the capacity of His servants and not needing their assistance, emphasizing His independence.
This previews the third wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: إن الله تعالى في تخليق الكفر والمعصية حكما لا يحيط بها الإحصاء :منها أن يتخلق ما حسن وقبح من الأفعال ليستدل على كمال قدرته ونفاذ مشيئته حيث قدر على تخليق المتضادين وإيجاد المتقابلين، وهذا آية كمال القدرة إذ من يوجد منه نوع واحد لا غير كان مضطرًا في ذلك، وبهذا كان خلق ما حسن من الأجسام وقبح وطاب وخبث ونفع وضر وآلم وألذ حكمة بالغة وتدبيرا صائبا فكذا هذا، وفي هذا زيادة أمر وهو إظهار القدرة على ما هو فعل غيره، وبه تمتاز القدرة القديمة من القدرة الحادثة والمشيئة الشاملة من المشيئة القاسرة، فيظهر بذلك أنه تعالى قادر على محل قدرة غيره متصرف في مقدور عباده مستبد بتحصيل مراده وغير مفتقر إليه محتاج إلى إعانته وهو الغني الحميد. ومنها : أنه تعالى بتخليقه الأفعال خيرها وشرها حسنها وقبيحها يتبين أنه ما يفعل لا يفعل عن حاجة ولا لجلب نفع ولا لدفع مضرة؛ إذ من ذلك فعله لا يفعل إلا لينتفع به. ومنها: أنه بذلك يظهر أنه تعالى غني عن خلقه عزيز بذاته لا يتعزز بكثرة أوليائه وأتباعه ولا يتقوى بأعوانه وأنصاره، ولا يضعف بتكاتف أحزاب
Then we say: Indeed God, in the creation of disbelief and disobedience, has wisdoms that cannot be enumerated: Among them is that He creates good and evil actions to be inferred from His perfect power and effective will, since He is able to create opposites and bring about contraries. And this is a sign of perfect power, because one from whom only one type of thing proceeds is constrained in that. And by this, the creation of good and evil bodies, pure and impure, beneficial and harmful, painful and pleasurable, was profound wisdom and sound management. So likewise this. And in this there is an additional matter: the manifestation of power over what is the act of another, and by this the eternal power (al-qudra al-qadīma) is distinguished from the temporal power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha), and the comprehensive will (al-mashī'a al-shāmila) from the limited will (al-mashī'a al-qāṣira). Thus it appears that He is powerful over the locus of power of another, disposing of the capacity of His servants, independent in attaining His desire, not needing their assistance, and He is the Rich, the Praised. And among them: that He, by creating actions, good and evil, beautiful and ugly, makes clear that He does not act out of need nor to gain benefit nor to repel harm; since whoever does that only acts to benefit from it. And among them: that by that it appears that He is free of need from His creation, mighty in Himself, not becoming mighty through the multitude of His saints and followers, nor becoming strong through His supporters and helpers, nor becoming weak by the alliance of parties.
Source pages p. 929

Commentary
This passage presents three wisdoms behind God's creation of evil actions like disbelief (kufr) and sin (maʿṣiya). The author first states that the wisdoms are beyond enumeration, then selects three. The first wisdom: By creating both good and evil actions, God demonstrates His perfect power and effective will. Creating opposites (like good and evil, pure and impure, beneficial and harmful) is a sign of complete power, because if only one type of thing proceeded from an agent, that agent would be limited and constrained. This also shows God's power over what is the act of another (i.e., His servants' acts), distinguishing the eternal power from temporal power and the comprehensive will from limited will. The second wisdom: By creating both good and evil actions, God shows that He acts not out of need or for benefit or harm prevention, because creatures act for their own benefit. The third wisdom: God's creation of opposites demonstrates His independence and self-sufficiency; He is not exalted by the number of His followers nor weakened by opposition.

Key Terms
تخليق الكفر والمعصية
كمال القدرة
المتضادين
المتقابلين
القدرة القديمة
القدرة الحادثة
المشيئة الشاملة
المشيئة القاصرة
الغني الحميد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's creation of evil implies deficiency in His power or goodness.
Correction: The text shows that creating both good and evil actually demonstrates perfect power, because only an all-powerful being can create opposites and contraries.

Checkpoint
What does the creation of opposites (good/evil, pure/impure) demonstrate according to the passage?
A) That God is limited.
B) That God's power is perfect.
C) That evil is an illusion.
D) That God needs creation.

Key Takeaway
God's creation of opposites, including good and evil actions, is a clear demonstration of His perfect power and distinguishes His eternal attributes from created limitations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience or witness evil, do you doubt God's power? How does this passage's argument that creating opposites is a sign of perfect power confront your doubt? What specific step will you take to remind yourself of this truth the next time you face suffering?
?
The passage distinguishes God's comprehensive will from limited will. Do you truly believe that God's will encompasses even your greatest failures and sins? If you did, how would your attitude toward your own shortcomings and repentance change right now?
?
God creates both good and evil to show His sovereignty. Are you willing to accept that even the evil in your own life—past hurts, current struggles—is part of His display of power and wisdom? What would it cost you to surrender your need to understand and simply trust that He is al-Ghani al-Hamid?

The Second Wisdom: God Acts Not from Need
The second wisdom for creating evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's creation of both good and evil actions shows He does not act out of need or for benefit.

Core Idea
God creates without need — He acts only to benefit, not to gain.

The author presents the second wisdom: by creating both good and evil actions, God demonstrates that He does not act out of need or to gain benefit or repel harm. Creatures act for their own benefit, but God is self-sufficient. This lesson explores that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for this wisdom. Notice it is one sentence encapsulating a profound point.
2
Understand the argument
The passage states that if someone acts out of need or for benefit, they do so to benefit themselves. God's creation of both good and evil shows He is not subject to such motives.
3
Reflect on God's self-sufficiency
Contrast this with created beings who act for their own interests. God's actions are not motivated by need.
This connects to the third wisdom about independence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: إن الله تعالى في تخليق الكفر والمعصية حكما لا يحيط بها الإحصاء :منها أن يتخلق ما حسن وقبح من الأفعال ليستدل على كمال قدرته ونفاذ مشيئته حيث قدر على تخليق المتضادين وإيجاد المتقابلين، وهذا آية كمال القدرة إذ من يوجد منه نوع واحد لا غير كان مضطرًا في ذلك، وبهذا كان خلق ما حسن من الأجسام وقبح وطاب وخبث ونفع وضر وآلم وألذ حكمة بالغة وتدبيرا صائبا فكذا هذا، وفي هذا زيادة أمر وهو إظهار القدرة على ما هو فعل غيره، وبه تمتاز القدرة القديمة من القدرة الحادثة والمشيئة الشاملة من المشيئة القاسرة، فيظهر بذلك أنه تعالى قادر على محل قدرة غيره متصرف في مقدور عباده مستبد بتحصيل مراده وغير مفتقر إليه محتاج إلى إعانته وهو الغني الحميد. ومنها : أنه تعالى بتخليقه الأفعال خيرها وشرها حسنها وقبيحها يتبين أنه ما يفعل لا يفعل عن حاجة ولا لجلب نفع ولا لدفع مضرة؛ إذ من ذلك فعله لا يفعل إلا لينتفع به. ومنها: أنه بذلك يظهر أنه تعالى غني عن خلقه عزيز بذاته لا يتعزز بكثرة أوليائه وأتباعه ولا يتقوى بأعوانه وأنصاره، ولا يضعف بتكاتف أحزاب
Then we say: Indeed God, in the creation of disbelief and disobedience, has wisdoms that cannot be enumerated: Among them is that He creates good and evil actions to be inferred from His perfect power and effective will, since He is able to create opposites and bring about contraries. And this is a sign of perfect power, because one from whom only one type of thing proceeds is constrained in that. And by this, the creation of good and evil bodies, pure and impure, beneficial and harmful, painful and pleasurable, was profound wisdom and sound management. So likewise this. And in this there is an additional matter: the manifestation of power over what is the act of another, and by this the eternal power (al-qudra al-qadīma) is distinguished from the temporal power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha), and the comprehensive will (al-mashī'a al-shāmila) from the limited will (al-mashī'a al-qāṣira). Thus it appears that He is powerful over the locus of power of another, disposing of the capacity of His servants, independent in attaining His desire, not needing their assistance, and He is the Rich, the Praised. And among them: that He, by creating actions, good and evil, beautiful and ugly, makes clear that He does not act out of need nor to gain benefit nor to repel harm; since whoever does that only acts to benefit from it. And among them: that by that it appears that He is free of need from His creation, mighty in Himself, not becoming mighty through the multitude of His saints and followers, nor becoming strong through His supporters and helpers, nor becoming weak by the alliance of parties.
Source pages p. 929

Commentary
This passage presents three wisdoms behind God's creation of evil actions like disbelief (kufr) and sin (maʿṣiya). The author first states that the wisdoms are beyond enumeration, then selects three. The first wisdom: By creating both good and evil actions, God demonstrates His perfect power and effective will. Creating opposites (like good and evil, pure and impure, beneficial and harmful) is a sign of complete power, because if only one type of thing proceeded from an agent, that agent would be limited and constrained. This also shows God's power over what is the act of another (i.e., His servants' acts), distinguishing the eternal power from temporal power and the comprehensive will from limited will. The second wisdom: By creating both good and evil actions, God shows that He acts not out of need or for benefit or harm prevention, because creatures act for their own benefit. The third wisdom: God's creation of opposites demonstrates His independence and self-sufficiency; He is not exalted by the number of His followers nor weakened by opposition.

Key Terms
تخليقه الأفعال
خيرها وشرها
حاجة
نفع
مضرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's creation of evil serves a need or benefits Him.
Correction: The passage shows that God does not act out of need or for benefit; He is self-sufficient.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does God not act out of need?
A) Because He is all-powerful.
B) Because creatures act for benefit, but God is self-sufficient.
C) Because He is compelled by fate.
D) Because He does not create evil.

Key Takeaway
God's creation of both good and evil reveals that He is absolutely free from any need or desire for benefit, unlike His creatures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know now that God does not need anything from you — not your worship, not your obedience, not your repentance. So why do you still hold back from Him? What is the real reason you are not more devoted to a Lord who is utterly independent of you? Write down one area where you act as if God needs your service, and resolve to change that intention today.
?
If God does not act out of need, then every good deed you do is not for His benefit but for yours. Are you grateful for that? Or do you secretly feel that God owes you something for your worship? Let this lesson strip away any sense of entitlement you carry. Commit to thanking Him for the privilege of serving Him, not because He needs it, but because you do.
?
The passage says creatures act only for their own benefit — but you are called to be like your Creator in selflessness. Where in your life are you acting only for your own gain, even in religious matters? Name one relationship or duty where you can act purely for God's sake, expecting nothing in return, and make a concrete plan to do that starting tomorrow.

The Third Wisdom: God's Independence and Self-Sufficiency
The third wisdom for creating evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God's creation of opposites demonstrates His independence from creation and His self-sufficiency.

Core Idea
God's creation of opposites shows He needs no supporters.

The third wisdom concludes that God's creation of both good and evil actions shows His independence. He is mighty in Himself, not by the multitude of followers, and not weakened by opposition. This lesson unpacks that point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the three negations: He does not become mighty through followers, nor strong through helpers, nor weak by opposition.
2
Identify the implications
This wisdom reinforces God's absolute self-sufficiency and might. He is not affected by creation's allegiance or enmity.
3
Connect to previous wisdoms
All three wisdoms together establish God's perfection and transcendence.
The passage ends with 'wa huwa al-ghani al-hamid' hinting at this.

First Wisdom: Manifesting Perfect Power and Independence
Nasafi presents the first wisdom: creation of opposites reveals God's perfect power and will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first wisdom behind God's creation of evil: it demonstrates His perfect power over opposites and His independence from His creation.

Core Idea
God's creation of opposites proves His power is complete and unrestricted.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi begins explaining the profound wisdoms behind why God creates evil actions such as disbelief and disobedience. The first wisdom focuses on how this very act showcases the perfection of God's power and the comprehensiveness of His will, distinguishing Him from limited beings. Let's read the passage to see how Nasafi argues this point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the translation. Notice how Nasafi structures his argument.
The passage contains several sub-points within this wisdom.
2
Identify the key concepts
Look for terms like 'opposites', 'perfect power', 'will', and 'independence'. Understand how they relate.
3
Understand the parallel with creation of diverse bodies
Nasafi draws an analogy with the creation of good and bad bodies to show that creating opposites is a sign of wisdom.
4
Notice the additional point about power over another's act
This wisdom also manifests God's power over what is the act of His servants, distinguishing eternal power from temporal.
This shows God's independence.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that God is powerful over the locus of another's power, independent, and praiseworthy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: إن الله تعالى في تخليق الكفر والمعصية حكما لا يحيط بها الإحصاء: منها أن يتخلق ما حسن وقبح من الأفعال ليستدل على كمال قدرته ونفاذ مشيئته حيث قدر على تخليق المتضادين وإيجاد المتقابلين، وهذا آية كمال القدرة إذ من يوجد منه نوع واحد لا غير كان مضطرًا في ذلك، وبهذا كان خلق ما حسن من الأجسام وقبح وطاب وخبث ونفع وضر وآلم وألذ حكمة بالغة وتدبيرا صائبا فكذا هذا، وفي هذا زيادة أمر وهو إظهار القدرة على ما هو فعل غيره، وبه تمتاز القدرة القديمة من القدرة الحادثة والمشيئة الشاملة من المشيئة القاصرة، فيظهر بذلك أنه تعالى قادر على محل قدرة غيره متصرف في مقدور عباده مستبد بتحصيل مراده وغير مفتقر إليه محتاج إلى إعانته وهو الغني الحميد. ومنها: أنه تعالى بتخليقه الأفعال خيرها وشرها حسنها وقبحها تبين أنه ما يفعل لا يفعل عن حاجة ولا لجلب نفع أو لدفع مضرة؛ إذ من ذلك فعله لا يفعل إلا ينتفع به. ومنها: أنه بذلك يظهر أنه تعالى غني عن خلقه عزيز بذاته لا يتعزز بكثرة أوليائه وأتباعه ولا يتقوى بأعوانه وأنصاره، ولا يضعف بتكاتف أحزاب أعدائه ولا يتضرر بتوفر عدد عصاته، بل هو الغني عن خلقه العزيز في ذاته المنيع في سلطانه القوي أيده المتين كيده
Then we say: Verily Allah Almighty, in the creation of disbelief (kufr) and disobedience (ma'siya), has wisdoms (hikam) that enumeration cannot encompass. Among them: that He creates what is good and evil of actions, so that His perfect power (qudra) and the penetration of His will (mashiyya) may be inferred, as He has power over creating opposites and bringing forth contraries. This is a sign of the perfection of power, for one from whom only one type issues is constrained in that. And by this, the creation of bodies that are good and evil, pure and impure, beneficial and harmful, painful and pleasurable, was profound wisdom and sound management. The same applies here. And in this there is an additional matter: the manifestation of power over what is the act of another. By this, the eternal power is distinguished from temporal power, and the comprehensive will from the deficient will. Thus it becomes apparent that He, exalted, is powerful over the locus of power of another, disposing of what His servants are capable of, independent in achieving His purpose, not needing their assistance—He is the Rich, the Praiseworthy. And among them: that He, exalted, by creating actions—their good and evil, their beauty and ugliness—makes it clear that He does not act out of need, nor to gain benefit, nor to repel harm. For one who acts out of that acts only for his own benefit. And among them: that by this it becomes apparent that He, exalted, is independent of His creation, mighty in His essence. He does not become mighty through the abundance of His friends and followers, nor does He gain strength through His helpers and supporters. He is not weakened by the unity of the parties of His enemies, nor is He harmed by the abundance of His disobedient ones. Rather, He is the Independent of His creation, the Mighty in His essence, the Invincible in His authority, the Strong in His support, the Firm in His plan.
Source pages p. 929

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of wisdoms (hikam) behind God's creation of evil acts like disbelief and disobedience. Nasafi begins by stating that the wisdoms are beyond enumeration, then lists three. The first wisdom: God creates both good and evil actions to demonstrate the perfection of His power and will, showing that He can bring opposites into existence. This is a sign of complete power because if only one type issued from Him, it would indicate constraint. He parallels this to the creation of diverse bodies (good/bad, pure/impure, etc.) which is also wise. Moreover, this creation manifests His power over what is another's act (i.e., the acts of servants), distinguishing eternal power from temporal power and comprehensive will from limited will. This proves God's independence: He disposes of His servants' capacities without needing their help. The second wisdom: by creating both good and evil actions, God shows that He does not act out of need, benefit, or self-interest—unlike creatures. The third wisdom: this demonstrates God's complete independence from creation: He is not glorified by many friends, strengthened by helpers, weakened by enemies, or harmed by the multitude of sinners. Instead, He is inherently mighty and independent.

Key Terms
كفر
معصية
حكمة
قدرة
مشيئة
متضادين
متقابلين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God creating evil means He needs evil or that His power is limited.
Correction: Rather, creating opposites demonstrates unrestricted power and independence. One who can only produce one type is constrained; God's ability to create opposites shows perfect power.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is a sign of perfect power in the context of creation?
A) Creating only good actions
B) Creating opposites (good and evil)
C) Creating nothing at all
D) Creating only evil actions

Key Takeaway
God's creation of both good and evil actions demonstrates His perfect power over opposites and His independence from need.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God creates even my acts of disobedience to manifest His perfect power, how does that challenge my pride and my sense of autonomy? What does it mean for you that your worst failures are still under His complete control and purpose?
?
The passage says God is not needful of our assistance. In what specific area of your life are you acting as if God needs your help to achieve His plan? What would change if you truly believed He is al-Ghaniyy, the Rich, and al-Hamid, the Praiseworthy?
?
The proof that God's power is perfect is that He creates opposites. How does this truth comfort you in the face of evil and suffering you see or experience? Does it make you trust Him more or challenge your assumptions? What is He calling you to submit to right now?

Second Wisdom: God Does Not Act Out of Need
Nasafi presents the second wisdom: creation of both good and evil shows God's freedom from need.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second wisdom: God's creation of good and evil shows He does not act out of need or for personal benefit.

Core Idea
God's creation of all actions proves His absolute self-sufficiency.

The second wisdom Nasafi presents draws on the fact that God creates both good and evil actions equally. This teaches us a crucial lesson about God's nature: He does not act out of any need or desire for benefit, unlike created beings who only act to gain something or avoid harm. Let's examine the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the short Arabic passage and its translation. Note its simplicity.
2
Understand the contrast
Nasafi contrasts God's actions with those of creatures: creatures act for need or benefit, God does not.
3
Reflect on the implication
This wisdom reinforces God's independence and self-sufficiency. Why would God create all actions if not for need?

Source Text

Among them: that He creates what is good and evil of actions, so that His perfect power (qudra) and the penetration of His will (mashiyya) may be inferred, as He has power over creating opposites and bringing forth contraries. And in this there is an additional matter: the manifestation of power over what is the act of another. He is not weakened by the unity of the parties of His enemies, nor is He harmed by the abundance of His disobedient ones. Rather, He is the Independent of His creation, the Mighty in His essence, the Invincible in His authority, the Strong in His support, the Firm in His plan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People might think God creates evil because He gains something from it or needs to create it for balance.
Correction: God is free of need and does not act for any benefit; His actions are purely for wisdom and purpose beyond our understanding.

Checkpoint
What does God's creation of both good and evil show about His actions?
A) He needs to create evil to balance good
B) He acts without need or benefit
C) He prefers evil over good
D) He is forced to create both

Key Takeaway
God's creation of all actions demonstrates He is free from need and does not act for personal benefit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God does not act out of need, what does that say about your own constant need for validation and approval? Are you living as though you are self-sufficient, forgetting that you are the one in need?
?
God creates both good and evil in your life, not for His benefit. How does that challenge your assumption that trials are meaningless? Will you trust His wisdom even when you see no benefit for yourself?
?
Your actions are created by God; you are not the ultimate origin. Does that thought humble you or frighten you? How will you realign your intention to seek only His pleasure, not your own gain?

Third Wisdom: God's Complete Independence from Creation
Nasafi presents the third wisdom: God's independence from creation is demonstrated by His creation of good and evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third wisdom: God's creation of both good and evil proves His absolute independence from His creation and from the actions of His servants.

Core Idea
God's glory is inherent, not dependent on followers or weakened by opponents.

The final wisdom in this passage emphasizes God's utter self-sufficiency. Nasafi explains that God does not gain might from many friends nor lose strength from many enemies. Instead, His independence is intrinsic to His essence. Let's read the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the list of things God does not depend on.
2
List what God does not need
Identify the phrases: 'friends', 'followers', 'helpers', 'supporters', etc. Understand they are all irrelevant to God's might.
3
Reflect on the attributes
The passage ends with attributes: al-Ghaniyy, al-Aziz, al-Mani', etc. Reflect on how these affirm independence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: إن الله تعالى في تخليق الكفر والمعصية حكما لا يحيط بها الإحصاء: منها أن يتخلق ما حسن وقبح من الأفعال ليستدل على كمال قدرته ونفاذ مشيئته حيث قدر على تخليق المتضادين وإيجاد المتقابلين، وهذا آية كمال القدرة إذ من يوجد منه نوع واحد لا غير كان مضطرًا في ذلك، وبهذا كان خلق ما حسن من الأجسام وقبح وطاب وخبث ونفع وضر وآلم وألذ حكمة بالغة وتدبيرا صائبا فكذا هذا، وفي هذا زيادة أمر وهو إظهار القدرة على ما هو فعل غيره، وبه تمتاز القدرة القديمة من القدرة الحادثة والمشيئة الشاملة من المشيئة القاصرة، فيظهر بذلك أنه تعالى قادر على محل قدرة غيره متصرف في مقدور عباده مستبد بتحصيل مراده وغير مفتقر إليه محتاج إلى إعانته وهو الغني الحميد. ومنها: أنه تعالى بتخليقه الأفعال خيرها وشرها حسنها وقبحها تبين أنه ما يفعل لا يفعل عن حاجة ولا لجلب نفع أو لدفع مضرة؛ إذ من ذلك فعله لا يفعل إلا ينتفع به. ومنها: أنه بذلك يظهر أنه تعالى غني عن خلقه عزيز بذاته لا يتعزز بكثرة أوليائه وأتباعه ولا يتقوى بأعوانه وأنصاره، ولا يضعف بتكاتف أحزاب أعدائه ولا يتضرر بتوفر عدد عصاته، بل هو الغني عن خلقه العزيز في ذاته المنيع في سلطانه القوي أيده المتين كيده
Then we say: Verily Allah Almighty, in the creation of disbelief (kufr) and disobedience (ma'siya), has wisdoms (hikam) that enumeration cannot encompass. Among them: that He creates what is good and evil of actions, so that His perfect power (qudra) and the penetration of His will (mashiyya) may be inferred, as He has power over creating opposites and bringing forth contraries. This is a sign of the perfection of power, for one from whom only one type issues is constrained in that. And by this, the creation of bodies that are good and evil, pure and impure, beneficial and harmful, painful and pleasurable, was profound wisdom and sound management. The same applies here. And in this there is an additional matter: the manifestation of power over what is the act of another. By this, the eternal power is distinguished from temporal power, and the comprehensive will from the deficient will. Thus it becomes apparent that He, exalted, is powerful over the locus of power of another, disposing of what His servants are capable of, independent in achieving His purpose, not needing their assistance—He is the Rich, the Praiseworthy. And among them: that He, exalted, by creating actions—their good and evil, their beauty and ugliness—makes it clear that He does not act out of need, nor to gain benefit, nor to repel harm. For one who acts out of that acts only for his own benefit. And among them: that by this it becomes apparent that He, exalted, is independent of His creation, mighty in His essence. He does not become mighty through the abundance of His friends and followers, nor does He gain strength through His helpers and supporters. He is not weakened by the unity of the parties of His enemies, nor is He harmed by the abundance of His disobedient ones. Rather, He is the Independent of His creation, the Mighty in His essence, the Invincible in His authority, the Strong in His support, the Firm in His plan.
Source pages p. 929

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of wisdoms (hikam) behind God's creation of evil acts like disbelief and disobedience. Nasafi begins by stating that the wisdoms are beyond enumeration, then lists three. The first wisdom: God creates both good and evil actions to demonstrate the perfection of His power and will, showing that He can bring opposites into existence. This is a sign of complete power because if only one type issued from Him, it would indicate constraint. He parallels this to the creation of diverse bodies (good/bad, pure/impure, etc.) which is also wise. Moreover, this creation manifests His power over what is another's act (i.e., the acts of servants), distinguishing eternal power from temporal power and comprehensive will from limited will. This proves God's independence: He disposes of His servants' capacities without needing their help. The second wisdom: by creating both good and evil actions, God shows that He does not act out of need, benefit, or self-interest—unlike creatures. The third wisdom: this demonstrates God's complete independence from creation: He is not glorified by many friends, strengthened by helpers, weakened by enemies, or harmed by the multitude of sinners. Instead, He is inherently mighty and independent.

Key Terms
غني
عزيز
أولياء
أتباع
أعوان
أعداء
عصاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God might need our worship or obedience to be powerful or to maintain His authority.
Correction: God is inherently mighty and independent; our actions do not affect His essence or power in any way.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does God's creation of good and evil show about His relationship with creation?
A) God needs creation to be mighty
B) God is independent and unaffected by creation
C) God is affected by the actions of His servants
D) God's power depends on His followers

Key Takeaway
God's creation of both good and evil reveals His complete independence from creation; He is not affected by obedience or disobedience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as though God's honor depends on your obedience? How does this passage challenge your assumption that your good deeds add to God's glory or that your sins diminish Him?
?
If God is not harmed by the abundance of disobedient ones, why do you spend so much energy worrying about what people think of your faith or fearing their rejection?
?
What would change in your relationship with God if you truly believed that His essence is mighty and independent regardless of your performance? Would you worship Him out of need or out of awe?
